[Our Newspaper Hangzhou, 11th] The lottery for conscription was held in the Hangzhou City Hall at 11:00 a.m. today. A total of 680 draftees were selected. Numbers were used in place of names, and the name list was sealed. After the lottery, applications for exemption or deferment of service can still be made based on the facts.

Ningbo to Establish a City; Drawings Submitted for Approval

Chen Zong'en Inspects Subordinate Counties

[Our Newspaper Hangzhou, 11th] The establishment of Ningbo as a city has attracted much attention from all parties. The central government has ordered that a map of the urban area be surveyed and submitted for approval. The local government has appointed Chen Zong'en as a special commissioner to oversee the matter. Chen plans to go to Yin County soon. With the reference of expert groups, the map can be completed in a few days. However, he must personally visit post offices in various counties before returning to Hangzhou.

Local News from Various Places

Fenghua News: The district general real estate tax reported by this newspaper is calculated based on the total amount of taxes and surcharges originally levied by the province and county in the 33rd year of the Republic. The provincial and county public grain taxes are reduced by half, and the landlords' accumulated grain is collected in full. The total area of the county is more than 5,300 square li, and the amount of grain that can be collected is 400,000 shi.

Ningbo News: In the area of Bailang Street, Jiangdong, there are many shoulder-carrying vendors who set up stalls on the streets to conduct business, which hinders traffic and the city's appearance. Relevant parties have instructed the Ningbo Police Bureau to ban them.

Jiading News: This county has slightly increased its land tax revenue and has specifically decided to start distributing funds for the national primary schools in each center for August on the 9th of this month. The funds for September will be distributed on a scheduled date.

Jintan News: The land price reported by this county was as high as more than 9 million yuan, which aroused opposition from the people throughout the county. After three careful deliberations, the originally set land price was uniformly reduced, with the highest being 6 million yuan per mu and the lowest being 3.6 million yuan. The registration deadline has been extended to the end of the month, and the evaluation of houses will not be reduced.

Songjiang News: On the 9th, the Tianmashan Police Substation saw a monk at the Tianqing Zen Temple in Shenxiang Third Bao. His behavior was suspicious, and a privately engraved wooden seal of the Songjiang County Government and a donation solicitation paper were found in his sleeve. A woman was also found hiding in the room. He is now being sent to the Joint Defense Command of the Five Counties of Songqing Jinjia Wu for interrogation.

Jiangyin News: The Xinong Yarn Factory in Huashu Town, eastern Jiangyin, caught fire at 7:00 a.m. on the 8th due to a generator catching fire, which spread to the cotton clothing and caused a major fire. The fire lasted for three hours, destroying ten factory buildings, more than ten pieces of cotton clothing, and machinery, resulting in a loss of approximately hundreds of millions.

Suxian News: This county strictly prohibits opium and other drugs and has set a deadline for elimination. The police station recently arrested more than 40 opium offenders, including Tan Shikuo, and sent them to the health center for compulsory detoxification.

Zhenhai News: The Third County Government Meeting resolved that, to facilitate the implementation of county administration, a joint meeting of township heads will be held on the 20th to discuss implementation methods.

Pinghu News: The Pingjia long-distance telephone from this county to Jiaxing has been decided to be set up independently by this county and must be completed before the 25th.

Dinghai News: The Shanghai Far East Commercial Shipping Company, to facilitate transportation on the Shanghai-Dingtai lines, will still use the company's 7-ton steel-hulled Hengyang transport vessel to participate in operations.

Commercial Slump, New Taxes Increase; Wuxi Business Community Pleads for Tax Postponement

[Our Newspaper Wuxi News] The trade associations of this county, including those for new medicines, Chinese medicines, silk fabrics, printing, jewelry, grain, and department stores, believe that the current commercial slump is a widespread phenomenon, and the various expenses are too numerous to list, making it difficult to maintain operations and leading to a precarious situation. As a result, business closures have occurred one after another. Recently, the tax bureau has introduced regulations for the collection of interest income tax, rental income tax, salary income tax, and other items. Businesses are unable to bear the burden and are pleading for relief. Moreover, the interest income tax is mostly due to businesses having to borrow money from various households on a temporary basis in order to cope with emergencies. As for the interest payable, it has already been paid. If the tax is pursued from various households again, it is practically impossible. In addition to the various businesses having to compensate, there is no other proper solution. Furthermore, the rental income tax and the current house tax seem to be redundant. This time, the rental income tax is levied on an annual basis rather than a monthly basis, which is extremely high. How can merchants bear this loss? Moreover, the salaries of shop assistants in various businesses are very low, far less than the wages of workers. If income tax is deducted, it will also be difficult for them to make ends meet. Yesterday, the above situation was jointly communicated to the Chamber of Commerce to forward it to the authorities, requesting them to sympathize with the difficulties of businesses and approve a temporary postponement of the collection of various new taxes to alleviate the suffering of the people.

Reader Opinions Regulations

(1) This column is absolutely open, and the authors are responsible for their own words. But avoid being lengthy. (2) Do not attack private individuals, and do not submit the same manuscript to multiple publications. (3) Contributors must indicate that the manuscript is a "Reader Opinion" and provide their real name and address, but a pseudonym may be used when publishing. (4) This newspaper does not pay for manuscripts. (5) This newspaper has the right to edit submissions. (6) Whether a manuscript is published or not will not be notified. (7) This newspaper may forward submissions to relevant agencies for reference when necessary.

A Police Officer Submits a Letter Expressing Grievances

First Letter We are all police officers standing in front of or downstairs of Guang Shengmen. Our families are suffering from the meager salaries we receive, suffering from cold and illness... And what about us? Bravely running in the cold wind and rain, on the icy and snowy ground, under the scorching sun, patiently standing at our posts, what is it for? When there is a fire, when there are bandits, we risk our lives to fight, arrest... what is it for? A few conspirators want to create a tragedy by using this hawker incident. We use our lives to protect the interests of the people, what is it for?

We certainly do not dare to claim credit, saying that we have fulfilled our responsibilities, but we let our families suffer and complain, and we ourselves endure and struggle, precisely because we want to take on a part of the national responsibility to protect the peace and tranquility of the society and the locality. So although it is a bit bitter, we feel a little comforted in spirit.

But some people say: "The police should serve the people and should not have the mentality of managing the people." Is this not serving the people but managing the people? Should we serve the bad elements or a few people, and let them disturb or hinder the interests or tranquility of the majority?

We shed blood for the interests of the majority... I ask, who sympathizes with us who are burnt out? Not only is there no sympathy or comfort, but we are also subjected to slander from some people due to misunderstanding?

Gentlemen! Try to put yourself in our shoes and think about how angry we will be, how difficult it will be to bear. So we want to appeal, we want to cry out, because we have been wronged? Because we have suffered unreasonable criticism, appeal, cry out, and ask the wise gentlemen to give us a little fair comfort! (A chief policeman representative from the Gaoqiao Police Station)

Second Letter I am a police officer and a loyal reader who reads your newspaper every day. In the November issue, your newspaper published the good news of a salary increase for civil servants and teachers, tripling the original salary. Now I still only receive 101,500 yuan per month. Fair gentlemen; not only have we not received a salary increase, but the five dou of yellow coarse rice (for October and November) that should be issued to us every month has not yet been issued. With prices rising, how can a salary of 100,000 yuan allow the police to maintain a living? Furthermore, civil servants are provided with military blankets, but we have not only not been provided with them but have also received no information at all. I wonder what the authorities are planning? The provision of goods at discounted prices sounds good, but each set costs 120,000 to 130,000 yuan. Please think about it, fair gentlemen, if we were to buy a set, we would have to go without food for at least a month, and we still wouldn't have enough. If there really are cheap goods available, where would we get the extra money to buy them? The police are the public servants of the people, protecting the people's lives and property, allowing them to live and work in peace. But with our current lives, fair gentlemen; give the police some sympathy! (Li Yaoxiang)

Civil Servants Should Receive Preferential Treatment on Transportation

In September of this year, the City Council and the free travel for civil servants and teachers case have not been implemented to this day. It is well known that the treatment of civil servants and teachers is meager and does not need to be repeated. Every day, they rely on one or two shuttle buses, limited by time and route. It is absolutely difficult to pick up and drop off all the civil servants scattered everywhere. Therefore, the number of people who can enjoy riding these shuttle buses is extremely small. The majority take trams or buses themselves. With the high cost of tickets today, this problem is serious for every civil servant. Fortunately, British and French tram companies have preferential measures for civil servants and teachers, selling monthly tickets for 10,000 yuan each, which greatly benefits the poor civil servants and teachers. However, in places where tram routes cannot reach, it is necessary to take the Public Utility Bureau's buses. Since the buses are operated by the city, they should be even more preferential, but the reality is completely the opposite. When civil servants of the City Government and its affiliated bureaus take the bus, they must buy tickets in accordance with the regulations, without any reduction. For employees of foreign tram companies in the same industry, there is no need to buy tickets under reciprocal conditions. Civil servants should absolutely abide by the law, and of course they must buy tickets when taking the bus. However, with prices rising and a monthly income of only more than 100,000 yuan, with the responsibility of supporting the family on their shoulders, the cost of transportation accounts for nearly one-third of the total income. How can they afford it? The organization and nature of buses and foreign tram companies are very different. They should do everything possible to seek benefits for civil servants and teachers. We no longer dream of the implementation of free travel for the Council. We only ask the Public Utility Bureau to quickly order the bus company, starting from January, to follow the example of tram companies and sell monthly tickets for civil servants and teachers to take the bus, and we will be very grateful! (A Small Civil Servant)

British Ship Strikes Mine in Corfu Strait; Britain Sends Ultimatum to Albania; Demanding Apology and Guarantee that Similar Incidents Will Not Occur Again; If No Satisfactory Reply Within Two Weeks, Complaint Will Be Filed with the Security Council

[Reuters, London, 10th] It was announced here tonight: The British government, regarding the loss of life and property caused by the unprovoked attack on British ships in the Corfu Strait, has sent a strongly worded ultimatum to the Albanian government, demanding a formal apology to Britain within fourteen days and requesting compensation for the damage. If a satisfactory reply is not received, the British government will submit the matter to the Security Council. The first incident occurred on May 15, when the British cruisers "Orion" and "Superb" were fired upon by Albanian coastal batteries while passing through the Strait, but fortunately were not damaged. Then, on October 22, the British destroyers "Saumarez" and "Volage" were seriously damaged after hitting underwater mines in the Strait, resulting in the deaths of as many as 44 officers and soldiers. In between the two incidents, merchant ships passing through the area were also frequently fired upon. The British government's note pointed out that British minesweepers swept mines in the area in November and discovered that these mines had been laid shortly before the British destroyers were attacked. From the perspective of Albania's strict coastal defense, if mines were laid in the Strait, the Albanian authorities would definitely know about it. Therefore, the British government believes that these mines were either laid by Albania itself, or the Albanian government must have known about the laying of the mines. Therefore, the Albanian government has seriously violated international law. The British government hereby demands that the Albanian government formally apologize to the British government for the attacks on British ships and guarantee that similar incidents will not occur again. The British government also demands that the Albanian government compensate for the losses suffered by the British ships on October 22 and pay full compensation to the families of the 44 officers and soldiers who died. If the Albanian government does not provide a satisfactory reply within fourteen days from the date of delivery of the note, the British government will regard Albania's actions as a serious threat to international peace and security and will file a complaint with the Security Council. The note was delivered to the Albanian Embassy in Belgrade yesterday.

Situation in the North Pacific and Mediterranean; Soviet Union Expresses Deep Concern; US and Soviet Foreign Ministers Hold Meeting; Four Foreign Ministers Reach Agreement on the Trieste Government Issue

[Our Newspaper Special Correspondent, New York, 11th] US Secretary of State Byrnes and Soviet Foreign Minister Molotov held a meeting today, during which Molotov made a very important statement. According to Molotov's statement to Byrnes, the Soviet Union has a "direct concern" in the entire North Pacific region and the Mediterranean, especially regarding the management of islands and colonies in those areas. Molotov also proposed a solution to this problem, stating that the US and the Soviet Union could exchange letters explaining the Soviet demands and its recognized rights. In short, the Soviet Union has broken its silence and clearly expressed its concern for Palestine, Italy, Libya, and the islands in the North Pacific north of the equator.

[Our Newspaper News] London, 11th Broadcast: The Four Powers Foreign Ministers Conference temporarily stopped discussing the German issue last night to wait for Molotov to receive new instructions from Moscow regarding the treaty procedures, and changed to discussing the Italian treaty. The Four Powers Foreign Ministers Conference is currently intensifying its work to clear up outstanding matters in the next few days and adjourn before Christmas.

[French News Agency, New York, 10th] The Four Foreign Ministers Conference has reached an agreement on all issues relating to the legal status of the Free Port of Trieste, except for one issue that has not been agreed upon, which has been decided to be postponed for discussion. According to experts who attended the Foreign Ministers Conference and participated in drafting the Trieste plan, if the economies of the countries behind Trieste, such as Austria, Hungary, and Czechoslovakia, can be revived and achieve a certain degree of balance, this step may enable the area to be self-sufficient in a few years. The political system of Trieste can be summarized as follows: (1) The Port of Trieste will be opened as a free port, jointly governed internationally, but without political power and with an autonomous nature. (2) The free port will be governed by a governor, but the governor must be nominated by the Trieste government committee and appointed by the chief executive of the area. (3) An international committee will be established, under the direction of the governor, consisting of one representative from Trieste, one representative each from the United Kingdom, the United States, the Soviet Union, France, Austria, Hungary, Poland, Czechoslovakia, and Switzerland. The chairman will be the representative from Trieste.

Security Council Discusses Greek Complaint; Soviet Proposal Rejected; Application for Membership Postponed for Discussion

[Reuters, Lake Success, 10th] The Security Council met today to discuss the issue of Siam's application for membership, deciding to postpone consideration until the next meeting. It then debated the Greek government's memorandum accusing Yugoslavia, Bulgaria, and Albania of supporting Greek guerrillas. It pointed out that this situation has caused friction between Greece and its neighbors, and if it is not quickly corrected, it may endanger international peace and security, so it requested an immediate investigation in the area. Greek Prime Minister Tsaldaris has come to New York in person to represent Greece.

[French News Agency, Lake Success, 11th] The Security Council discussed the Greek complaint today. The Soviet Union proposed inviting representatives from Bulgaria and Yugoslavia to participate in the discussion immediately, but without the right to vote. The proposal was rejected. At the same time, the Security Council unanimously passed a resolution inviting Greece to make a statement on the matter. Then, the issue of whether Greece's complaint was a "dispute" between Greece and its neighbors was discussed. It was immediately decided to postpone inviting representatives from Albania and Bulgaria to participate in the discussion until the Security Council decides on this issue. Finally, it was stipulated that Greece and Yugoslavia would participate in the discussion, but without the right to vote. The Albanian and Bulgarian representatives would be invited to participate in the discussion when the Security Council decides that this issue is a "dispute."

Independence of People in Trusteeship Areas; Must Stipulate a Definite Date; Indian Representative Finally Withdraws Proposal

[Our Newspaper News] London, 11th Broadcast: The Indian representative recently proposed in the UN General Assembly Committee that each of the eight trusteeship agreements currently under consideration should stipulate a definite date by which the trustee country should relinquish all sovereignty over the trusteeship territory. In other words, the Indian representative aims to fight for a definite period of time to allow the people of the trusteeship territory to become independent. However, the countries in charge of the trusteeship areas strongly opposed this proposal, and the resolution was withdrawn. However, Indian representative Menon made a statement stating that he would re-submit this proposal after the United Nations Trusteeship Council is formally established.

The United Nations General Assembly Has Approved the Budget for This Year

Totaling More Than Eighteen Million US Dollars

[Central News Agency, New York, 10th] The Administrative and Budgetary Committee of the United Nations General Assembly today voted to approve the UN budget for the year 1946 at $18,912,792. The committee also preliminarily approved a budget for the year 1947 at $21,936,771.

UNRRA Holds Plenary Session, Emphasizes Future Relief Work, LaGuardia Defends UNRRA Work, Says Food Distribution Never Involved Politics

[United Press, Washington, 10th] As UNRRA's European operations will conclude at the end of this month and its Far Eastern operations at the end of March next year, representatives from the 48 member nations of UNRRA convened a plenary session here today. Director-General LaGuardia strongly defended UNRRA's food distribution efforts, stating that any claims of political manipulation in UNRRA's allocation of food were absolutely incorrect. He asserted that he was completely unaware of any political involvement in food distribution. LaGuardia recounted that all UNRRA food shipments were decided by a nine-nation Management Committee. He stated he had heard no objections from any government regarding political involvement in food distribution. LaGuardia's statement was in response to Under Secretary of State Acheson's remarks on Sunday, in which Acheson claimed some countries received too much aid while others received too little, calling it a significant error.

[United States Information Service, Washington, 10th] UNRRA Director-General LaGuardia today submitted a report on UNRRA's work during the third quarter of 1946 to the sixth session of the UNRRA Council. According to the report, as of November 18, 72% of UNRRA's work plan had been completed. In total, UNRRA had shipped approximately 17,845,000 long tons (18,130,520 metric tons) of relief supplies worth $2,117,653,000. The main issue now is the continuing plan after UNRRA formally concludes its relief efforts for Europe on December 31st of this year and for China on March 31st of next year.

Investigation of National Armed Forces Case, A Debate at the United Nations General Assembly, Agreement on Nine Principles for Disarmament Issues, Subcommittee Drafts Report for General Assembly Discussion

[United Press, Lake Success, 10th] British representative Noel-Baker today urged Soviet Foreign Minister Molotov in the United Nations General Assembly to endorse the plan for investigating foreign and domestic armed forces, stating that "we should allow the facts to be made public, to lift the veil and see what is happening in all countries of the world, in order to dispel suspicion." He urged the Soviet Union not to follow a policy of isolation, which breeds suspicion. Shaw also claimed that Molotov was opposing his own proposal. When the Political Committee passed the armed forces investigation case by a vote of 34 to 7, the Soviet Union expressed its dissent, stating that the issue of investigating domestic troop numbers was only related to the general disarmament case. Earlier, US representative Connally also stated, "We have no secrets. We should make all our military strength public to the world, and we hope other countries can do the same." However, Connally reiterated his opposition to the British proposal to have the Security Council send an investigative team to review troop deployment reports on the ground.

[United Press, Lake Success, 11th] The United Nations General Assembly today continued to discuss the issue of investigating national armed forces. The Soviet representative agreed that an international organization should be responsible for investigating national armed forces, but insisted that investigations of national armaments, including atomic bombs, must occur simultaneously, thus merging the investigation of armed forces and armaments into one case. The British representative has "in principle" already approved the method proposed by the Soviet Union. If this proposal is passed by the General Assembly, the United States will inevitably have to disclose its atomic bomb secrets. The main point of contention at present remains the issue of veto power. The British representative insists that the international organization responsible for investigating national armed forces and armaments should not be subject to the veto power in the Security Council, while the Soviet representative argues the opposite. General Assembly President Spaak declared that if this proposal is passed by the General Assembly, the entire organization for investigating national armed forces and armaments could be established by January 15th of next year.

[Agence France-Presse, Lake Success, 10th] The drafting subcommittee of the Political and Security Committee of the United Nations General Assembly is scheduled to hold its final meeting tomorrow to draft a report to be submitted to the Political and Security Committee. If passed, it will then be submitted to the General Assembly for discussion. However, according to well-informed sources, an agreement has been reached on all the key points to be included in the draft resolution, including: (1) accelerating the work of the United Nations Atomic Energy Commission; (2) the Security Council should promptly review the reports submitted by the Atomic Energy Commission; (3) recognizing the necessity of limiting and reducing national armaments and armed forces; (4) drafting several agreements to prohibit atomic weapons and other weapons of mass destruction; (5) establishing an international control organization under the jurisdiction of the Security Council, with its powers and duties also defined by the Security Council in a military agreement, subject to the approval of all members of the United Nations; (6) members of the United Nations should promptly provide the necessary troops to the Security Council for command in order to form an international army; (7) members of the United Nations stationed within the borders of former enemy countries should gradually withdraw their troops in progressive and proportional percentages; (8) members of the United Nations stationed within the borders of non-enemy countries should withdraw their troops unless they have obtained the consent of the latter's government; (9) universally reducing armed forces of all countries. Regarding the last point, the subcommittee held lengthy discussions because it not only stipulated that domestic armed forces should be reduced, but also that the troops gradually withdrawn by member states from other countries should also be reduced. Finally, the British representative proposed an amendment requesting that each United Nations member state provide precise reports on its armaments and military strength, which was approved by the subcommittee.

Agreement Draft between the United Nations and the Universal Postal Union Under Discussion

[Central News Agency, New York, 11th Dispatch] Experts from thirty-eight countries held a meeting here today to study the draft agreement between the Universal Postal Union and the United Nations, which was drafted by the United Nations Secretariat. During today's meeting, many speakers considered several parts of the draft to be quite commendable. British expert Wheatman stated that a valuable contribution that the Universal Postal Union could make, and one that could assist the United Nations in maintaining world peace, is to deprive aggressors of the ability to exchange postal items with other countries.

US Fleet Commander Discusses Future Warfare, Arctic Is Important But Coast Should Also Be Emphasized

[United Press, New York, 10th] Vice Admiral Barbey, a Pacific landing warfare expert and commander of the Fourth Fleet, today discussed future warfare trends. According to him, if the United States is attacked by weapons of mass destruction in the future, 5 million people may be killed or injured within a few hours. But the enemy cannot defeat us all at once. Within hours, our country will implement large-scale retaliatory attacks. The United States is at least ten years ahead of other countries in the manufacture of weapons of mass destruction, but we must buy them unceasingly. Military progress is the most powerful guarantee behind the success of the United Nations. If war breaks out again one day, it will never be a gentleman's duel, but a matter of the survival of the civilized masses. In general, people emphasize attacks coming across the Arctic. I do not know the reason for this. I believe that it is more possible for foreign countries to send more than a dozen submarines and atomic bombs from locations scattered hundreds of miles away in the Atlantic Ocean to various cities on the east coast of the United States. Rocket-style atomic bombs can even be launched after the submarine sinks, but our retaliation will also be swift. The enemy cannot avoid it and will suffer even greater losses.

China and India (Part 2)

— (Written by Nehru)

Translated by Zhou Xiangguang, Our Correspondent in India

Xuanzang tells us a lot about the situation at Nalanda University, and other records are similar. A few years ago, I visited Nalanda University and was amazed to see many relics that had been systematically excavated from the ruins. Today, only a small portion has been excavated, and the rest is still inhabited by people, but these places still include vast gardens surrounded by solemn houses made of stone.

Shortly after Xuanzang passed away in China, another traveler, the monk Yijing, came to India. He set out from China in 671 AD and traveled for a full two years before reaching the port of Tamralipta in India, which is at the mouth of the Hooghly River. Because he came by sea, he stopped in Palembang (in Sumatra) and studied some months of Chuo Wen. This sea voyage was of great significance, perhaps due to changes in the political situation that made Central Asia unstable, making it impossible to come by land. Several Buddhist monasteries along the way were places for them to stop and rest. Sea routes may also be more suitable for the growth of Indian colonies in Indonesia and for establishing regular commercial relations between India and other countries. Records from Yijing and others show that at this time, there was regular navigation between Iran, India, Malaya, Sumatra, and China. Yijing first traveled from Guangdong to Sumatra by Persian ship.

Yijing also studied at Nalanda University for a long time and brought back thousands of Sanskrit classics. His main interest was in the key points of Buddhist rituals and rules, and he recorded these things in great detail. He also told us a lot about clothing, food, and customs. The main food in North India was wheat, as it is now, and in East India, rice was the main food. Meat was sometimes eaten, but it was rare. Ghee, milk, and other things could be seen everywhere, and there were many biscuits and fruits. Yijing recorded something extremely important for Indians, which is the reliance on the purity of a specific religious ritual. "Now the first and most important distinction between the five Indias and other countries is the sincerity of religious rituals. Moreover: 'Leftover food, which can be stored in China, may not conform to Indian regulations'."

Yijing once talked about India, saying that it is the West, but he himself tells us that India is called Aryadesha. The meaning of Arya is "struggle", and the meaning of Desha is "land", so it is the "land of struggle", all for the West. It is so named because the character of its people is noble and pure, and all the people praise this land with this name. India is also called "Central Land" (Madhyadesha) because it is located in the center of all the countries. All people feel close to this name. The northern barbarians (such as the Huns, Mongols, Turks) only call it Jingtǔ as India, but this is not a common word after all. This is just a local name and has no special meaning. The people of India do not know this name, and the most appropriate name for India is "Pure Land."

Yijing's discussion of Shendu is very interesting. He once said: "Some people say that the meaning of India (Indu) is the moon, and the Chinese call India as Yindu, which comes from this. Although its meaning may be like this, this is not a common name. Likewise, when Indians call China as Zhina, it's just a name and has no special meaning." He also mentioned the names used for Korea and other countries in Sanskrit.

Yijing has the utmost respect for India, and the same goes for Indian things. He described these things in detail and gave them to his motherland—China—first. India may be the "Pure Land," but China is the "Divine Land." "The people of the Five Indias are quite proud of their sincerity and nobility. But the reverence for thought, literacy, dignified demeanor, moderate attitude, welcoming etiquette, the deliciousness of food and soup, and the kind and just heart can only be obtained in China, not in other countries." The healing skills of acupuncture and the ingenuity of pulse detection cannot be replaced by any place in India, and the medicines that prolong life can only be seen in China... In terms of human character and the quality of things, China is named the Divine Land. Which of the Five Indias does not respect China?"

The ancient Sanskrit term for the Chinese emperor is Deva-Putra, which is accurately translated as the "Son of Heaven."

Yijing himself was a Sanskrit scholar. He praised Sanskrit and said that this language is also revered in the distant countries of the north and south. There are also several people from Shenzhou (China) and Heaven (India) who teach the rules of this language. Sanskrit scholars in China must have been extremely common. We find it interesting that several Chinese scholars wanted to use Sanskrit phonetic symbols in the Chinese language. One of the best examples is the monk Shouwen of the Tang Dynasty in China, who wanted to make the Chinese language an alphabetic phonetic language in this direction. The influence of Indian Buddhism is subtle. Although there are often pilgrims from China who come to visit the Buddhist holy sites in India, the actual academic exchanges between the two countries have been cut off. When the political revolution took place in the 11th century AD, all the Buddhist monks took the classics and went to Nepal or crossed the Himalayas to Tibet. We already knew that important parts of ancient Indian writings had reached China and Tibet, and in recent years, the original texts have been completely discovered there, and there are quite a few translations. Many ancient Indian classics, not only those about Buddhism, but also those about Brahmanism, astronomy, mathematics, and medicine, are still preserved in Chinese and Tibetan. Regarding these academic connections, the best example that still exists today is the Sanskrit, Tibetan, and Chinese dictionary of Buddhist terms. This book was written in the 9th or 10th century AD, and is called the Great Dictionary (Mahavyutpatti).

Page 5

Lu Jingshi Convenes Representatives of Textile Workers to Discuss the Issue of Annual Bonus Distribution, Labor Expresses Concessions, Hoping to Still Follow the Methods of Previous Years, The Social Affairs Bureau Will Convene Business Leaders to Hold Talks

[Our Correspondent] Lu Jingshi, Director of the Organization and Training Department of the Ministry of Social Affairs, yesterday afternoon convened representatives of cotton textile workers at the conference room of the Social Affairs Bureau to exchange views on the issue of annual bonuses. Director Lu told reporters: the labor side believes that the profits of the cotton textile industry are very high, and hopes to have an annual bonus of six months' salary; but the business side believes that yarn prices have been restricted, and profits are limited. Although the books show money, if calculated in terms of materials, it has not increased, and it cannot accept the labor side's request. After his persuasion, the labor side is willing to make considerable concessions, but the minimum hope is to follow the methods of previous years, dividing the annual bonus of workers into 20%, 25%, and 33% of the total annual income, with workers getting 20% and management personnel getting 30%. The so-called total annual income refers to the actual income after deducting holidays. He believes that the labor and management sides of the cotton textile industry will definitely be able to work together harmoniously, and reach an agreement on this issue under the principles of maintaining production and protecting labor. In addition, according to labor representatives, yesterday's meeting was an informal exchange of views, and the labor side has put forward its views as much as possible for reference. Lu will return to Nanjing tomorrow and will come to Shanghai again on the 21st of this month, at which time there should be a concrete decision on the annual bonus issue for the cotton textile industry.

It is also learned that Wu Kaixian, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, has scheduled a talk with the standing directors of the city's General Labor Union, Industry Association, and Chamber of Commerce at 4:00 PM on Friday, the 13th of this month. Notices have already been issued, and it is hoped that they will all attend at that time.

Discussion on Relief for the Unemployed Postponed to Next Week

[Our Correspondent] The Social Affairs Bureau originally scheduled a meeting yesterday to discuss a plan for providing relief to unemployed workers, but it was temporarily unable to be held due to unforeseen circumstances and was decided to be postponed to next Monday. According to Li Jianhua, Deputy Director of the Bureau, the workers' hostel was originally scheduled to accommodate more than 1,000 workers, but the current actual number of residents is over 1,800. Due to overcrowding, environmental hygiene has been greatly affected, resulting in more than a dozen worker children dying of smallpox in November. At the meeting next week, discussions will be held on how to improve the hostel's medical and health facilities, and the issue of raising this funding. As for the placement of unemployed workers, Li believes that the palliative measures are to enable factories that have already started work to maintain production, and to enable those that have not started work to resume work as soon as possible. The fundamental solution is to improve the entire national economy in order to increase employment opportunities.

Patrolling and Inspecting the Restricted Construction Zone; Kindly Advising the Removal of Makeshift Sheds; More Than 100 Mu of Vacant Land in Five Locations to Be Leased to Slum Dwellers

[Report from Our Newspaper] Regarding the makeshift sheds being built within the city's restricted construction zone, the Municipal Government, after a resolution at the municipal meeting to prohibit them, the Bureau of Public Works, upon order, began patrolling and enforcing regulations yesterday in conjunction with the Police Bureau.

Yesterday at 9:00 AM, the two bureaus specially formed a mobile patrol team, led by Song Xueqin, Section Chief of the Demolition Section of the Bureau of Public Works, and Lu Xia, Section Chief of the Traffic Section of the Police Bureau, leading six police officers and six craftsmen each, set out on patrol. Before the patrol personnel departed, they were specially summoned for instruction by Zhao Shekang, Director of the Bureau of Public Works, who instructed all personnel to advise the residents of the makeshift sheds to dismantle them with a sincere and kind attitude, and to inform them of the reasons for the demolition, the relationship to the interests of the public, and the resettlement arrangements, so as to provide a way out for the residents. The patrol team inspected Changning Road and Kaixuan Road in the morning and went to Yangshupu and the Suzhou River area in the afternoon. There were more structures built in the Yangshupu area, while the situation on the other roads was better. When the patrol personnel saw a small number of slum dwellers building houses, they explained the demolition matter to them. The slum dwellers' attitude was very good, and they all agreed to dismantle them within two or three days. The craftsmen and police officers accompanying them did not order immediate demolition yesterday but gave warnings that if they were not dismantled within the time limit, they would be demolished on their behalf.

At the same time, Zhao, the Director of the Bureau of Public Works, personally visited Changshou Road, Xikang Road, Yuyao Road, Yichang Road, and Jiangning Road yesterday morning together with Wang Yuankang, the Director of the Construction Department of the Bureau. The site with the most houses built was Yuyao Road (formerly Singapore Road), and most of the central district's shacks were built within the roads or alleys. Director Zhao will still personally inspect the Yangshupu area today. Yesterday, our reporter paid a special visit to Director Zhao, asking him about the methods for dealing with the slum dwellers, and he informed us that the makeshift sheds within the restricted construction zone that have not yet been completed will definitely be demolished, and they will now be directed to build in non-restricted construction zones. At the same time, according to urban planning, the municipal government has approved and instructed the Land Administration Bureau to slightly purchase five private land locations totaling one hundred and sixty-three mu to build civilian villages, including: 21 mu on Feihong Road in Yangshupu, 45 mu in Caojiadu in the Pusong District, 40.8 mu on Tianyaoqiao in the Hunan District, 15.6 mu in Yangjiabo in Pudong, and 40.8 mu on Zhaoju Road in the Hunan District. The land was originally intended to be included in next year's budget for the construction of civilian villages. However, before the funds are available, the vacant land can be leased to slum dwellers for site selection.

More than one hundred buildings in the civilian village built by the Bureau in Damuqiao, Nanshi, are now rented by a small number of citizens, and the rest are used by municipal government employees. Director Zhao also stated that housing construction must be zoned to match urban planning. If dormitories can be built near factories, the housing shortage problem can be alleviated somewhat. Residential and commercial areas are also often divided. Director Zhao also inspected the bottleneck-shaped protruding houses in the city yesterday, and this issue will be submitted for public discussion at the next municipal meeting.

Makeshift sheds with bamboo pillars, plank walls, and straw roofs (Photo by Yu Chuangshuo of our newspaper)

Meng Jiangnu Performance Successful; Madame Chiang Hosts Tea Party for Sponsors; Mei Lanfang Critiques Acting; Fei Xi Praises the Plot

Madame Chiang Soong Mei-ling hosted a tea party at the Second Reception Hall of the Lizi Society at 5:00 PM yesterday to raise funds for the reconstruction of the maternal school for the veterans of the National Revolutionary Army, inviting the Shanghai sponsors of the Meng Jiangnu opera performance. Foreign guests Fei Xi and Mayor Wu's couple, Fang Zhi, Xu Jiqing, Wu Shaodui, Xuan Tiewu, Huang Renlin, Wei Jingmeng, Xi Yushu, Ding Guitang, Liu Gongyun, Xu Xueyu, Cao Jun, Mei Lanfang, Wang Bosheng, Deng Shiping, Guo Linshuang Liu Jingji, Zhang Rongchu, Shen Dexie, Wang Zhaohuai, Zhang Chu and more than 20 others attended. Despite the torrential rain, Madame arrived on time and shook hands and greeted the guests one by one, with a very happy mood. After the guests and hosts had some refreshments, Madame first consulted Dr. Mei Lanfang and Wang Bosheng, the president of the National Drama School, separately for their criticisms of the content of the Meng Jiangnu opera. They believed that in addition to the need for slight improvements in performance skills, the plot was deeply meaningful and could express a part of Chinese culture.

Then, General Secretary Huang Renlin reported briefly, saying that he was very grateful for the enthusiastic fundraising from all walks of life for the Shanghai performance of the Meng Jiangnu opera. Judging from the situation of the continuous performances, the total income may reach 400 million. Among the sponsors, especially Mr. Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, and Xu Jikang provided the most assistance. Mr. Mei Lanfang and Wang Bosheng provided the most guidance, so that such achievements could be obtained, which is really a rare opportunity. The evening show on the 10th was sold out, and it was originally scheduled to close on the evening of the 11th. In order to satisfy the audience's interest, a special performance was added on the 12th, and the ticket prices for the daytime show were reduced to 2,000 and 4,000, and the ticket prices for the evening show were reduced to 5,000 and 10,000, so that ordinary citizens can watch it. After Huang's report, Madame Chiang delivered a speech.

Madame Chiang then rose to give a speech, saying that the Meng Jiangnu opera has achieved great success in Shanghai. She not only represents the veterans' schools in expressing gratitude to everyone for raising educational funds for our veterans' children, but also feels that it is of profound significance to introduce Chinese culture to foreign countries and increase international understanding through the Meng Jiangnu opera, and she feels sincerely gratified. After the Meng Jiangnu opera was staged, she and Chairman Chiang watched the performance four times and felt that the content of the opera was much improved compared to ordinary old dramas. General Marshall was also interested in the opera and often talked about it, which proves that the opera can attract many audiences if it is performed abroad.

Sponsors' Opinions

Then, each of the sponsors stated their opinions on improving the opera, which can be summarized into the following points: (1) The music must match the movements, (2) The actress playing Meng Jiangnu is too old, (3) Gods and ghosts are mixed together, and the movements are messy, (4) The makeup should be improved to distinguish between good and evil. Finally, Madame asked the foreign guest Fei Xi for his opinion. He said that the plot was very good and hoped that it could be performed in Washington, New York and other places in the United States. Madame expressed her approval, and then General Secretary Huang made a concluding remark, saying that everyone's enthusiastic sponsorship has not only made a great contribution to cultural work, but also laid the foundation for the future of the veterans' schools, and he expressed his great gratitude to everyone. The guests and hosts talked happily until about 6:00 PM, and then dispersed in joy. After the meeting, Madame, accompanied by Huang Renlin, inspected the various venues in the reception hall for a week before taking a car back to her official residence on Dongping Road to rest. At 8:30 PM, Madame went to the Nanjing Grand Theater to watch the Meng Jiangnu performance again, with great interest, and returned at the end.

The Person in Charge of the Troupe Said That the Number of People Will Be Reduced When Going Abroad

Also, according to Deng Shiping, the general manager of the China Youth Music Troupe, the play was performed at the Lizi Society in Nanjing for nine days from November 6, and there were many audiences. The ticket prices were divided into two types: 10,000 and 50,000, and the income was more than 100 million yuan. It has been performed in Shanghai since December 5, and the ticket prices are divided into three types: 10,000, 20,000, and 50,000. The total income will be settled after the performance is over. The results are generally not bad. However, there are still many shortcomings in the plot content and performance skills, and he hopes that people from all walks of life will give more guidance and sponsorship. The troupe sincerely accepts and earnestly improves. When asked about the total number of actors, he said that there are 35 actors and about 60 people including transportation and other affairs. In the future, if performing abroad, they will still try their best to reduce the number.

Meeting Taixu in the Jade Buddha Temple; Abbot of Buddhist Sects Mournfully

[Special feature from our newspaper] In the cold rain, with the sound of Buddhist chanting, the Jade Buddha Temple appears even more quiet and solemn.

Master Songyue led us through a corridor, and stopped in front of a quiet hall on the rear side of the Great Buddha Hall. He stepped forward and said with a smile:

"This is the old Dharma Master Taixu."

The old Dharma Master Taixu was wearing a robe of yellowish-brown, with the cuffs of his white flannel undershirt extending outside the cuffs of the robe. He was wearing a velvet hat, also dark brown. Behind his tortoiseshell-rimmed glasses were a pair of kind and joyful eyes, looking at us with a smile. He extended his plump and slender hand and shook ours happily. We sat down on the comfortable sofas. Master Songyue sat quietly on a chair beside us, listening.

Buddhism prohibits killing, and a large-scale war of mutual slaughter is about to take place, so naturally, we inevitably talked about the current situation. The old Dharma Master seemed to hesitate for a moment, and then slowly said, "Since the 26th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1937], the Kuomintang finally won the War of Resistance, and in fact, the whole country should be able to recuperate and stabilize. Who knew—the negotiations would fail to produce results, leading to this situation!"

The old Dharma Master lowered his head and could not help but nod.

Buddhist Party Formation

We changed the subject: "Recently, there has been a widespread rumor about the formation of a Buddhist party. What is the Grand Master's view?"

"I discussed this issue in the first issue of the Juequn Weekly. Zhongshan Xisheng said that political power belongs to all the people, and monks and nuns are also people, so they should be willing to ask about political affairs. We can participate in elections, to the Senate, the Provincial Council, or the National Assembly—but I don't advocate the formation of a party."

Dharma Master Taixu has always been very concerned about Buddhist education. In Chongqing, he presided over the Haizang Institute of Buddhist Studies, which played a very important role in the border areas.

Speaking of Tibetan Buddhism, I can't help but think of Esoteric Buddhism, because the various miracles of Living Buddha Nuona in Shanghai are really too strange. The Dharma Master said: Esoteric Buddhism is indeed a bit strange, but it is indeed Mahayana. Some strange things can be said to be "techniques," but what the Haizang Institute of Buddhist Studies studies are "doctrines," which are "learning."

Jing'an Temple Incident

After breakfast, we talked about the Jing'an Temple incident, which has attracted a lot of attention.

Dharma Master Tai Lu scratched his head, which was already full of silver threads. He said firmly:

"I think this matter includes two parts. The first part is the matter of De Wu and Mi Jia being reported as traitors. Honestly speaking, it is not really enough to consider these two people as traitors. If anyone who participated in one or two people's organizations during the enemy's occupation is considered a traitor, I am afraid that there are four or five million people in the occupied areas who should be reported. The second part is the issue of how to manage Jing'an Temple and a little of its property. I think that the management system in temples in the past is no longer suitable for modern times. The Haizang Institute of Buddhist Studies that I established in Chongqing was originally a desolate temple. Because the management in the temple was poor, it was very damaged. Later, when the Institute of Buddhist Studies was established, a board of directors was established to manage the temple property, and a specialist was hired to be responsible for the affairs of the Institute, which achieved results. I think the property of Jing'an Temple can also be organized into a board of directors to manage it, and a hospital, library, or school can be run on the temple grounds, and another specialist can be hired to be responsible for managing administrative matters—it can be run as a business run by Buddhism. This is probably a more appropriate method."

On Monk Liugen

Jing'an Temple is currently managed by Liugen, but the Dharma Master clearly believes that the current method is not a fundamental solution. He said: "In the future, when De Wu and the others return, there will definitely be disputes. Liugen is a mediocre and incompetent person. He also presided over Jing'an Temple in the early years of the Republic of China, but he has never managed it well since he came. Lawsuits have never stopped. Therefore, the management method at the root must be improved."

The Dharma Master is already fifty-eight years old this year. In recent years, because of high blood pressure, he cannot write too many articles or say too much. He may be going to Ningbo soon. The National Buddhist Association meeting to be held in Nanjing next year will also be presided over by the Dharma Master.

When we left the Jade Buddha Temple, the twilight in the rain was already very dim.

Dharma Master Tai Lu meeting reporters (Photo by Lu Shunxing of our newspaper)

Coal Supply Has Improved; Sources Are Actively Being Dredged; 6,000 Tons of Annam White Coal Will Be Shipped

According to the person in charge of the Fuel Management Committee of the Ministry of Economic Affairs in the Shanghai District: In order to prevent the black market for coal in the city, the method of allocating coal to factories has been improved this month, that is, in the past, the required amount for each factory per month was declared by the Coal Industry Association on behalf of its members. Now, it has been changed to factories directly submitting a list of their actual needs, which is then reviewed and allocated by the Association. On the one hand, it can cooperate with the needs of factories to speed up production, and on the other hand, it can avoid the Association from manipulating the process, so that the black market price will naturally tend to decline. In terms of white coal, it is estimated that 6,000 tons may be shipped from Annam on the 15th. According to reliable sources, a considerable amount has been negotiated with the Annam Gubao Coal Mine, and if there are no accidents, 6,000 tons can be shipped to China every month, and a batch can arrive by the end of the month. In terms of lump coal, there is a shortage of goods in various countries after the war, and merchants are freely purchasing many tons. The Association has previously negotiated the purchase of 10,000 tons from the United States, and if the crew strike there subsides, it can be shipped. The distribution method will be determined separately.

Relieving the Coal Shortage Depends on Opening Up New Sources

The person in charge continued: In order to solve the current difficulty in the raw materials for coal briquettes, in addition to ensuring the regular supply of raw materials, another 2,000 tons of small pieces of white coal will be added to the Coal Briquette Industry Association this month to supplement the raw materials. Regarding the elimination of the general black market problem, it is still hoped that the local government will do its best to assist. The person in charge finally said: Relieving the coal shortage depends on opening up new sources, the most important of which is the transportation problem. According to the arrival of goods from various places from March to September in the past, they were all ideal. The results in October and November were not good. Within the scope of ability, we will try our best to strengthen it. In addition to maintaining 145,000 tons per month on the source side, more than 50,000 tons in Taiwan are allocated to transportation, water and electricity agencies, and factories, etc. The Resources Committee is paying special attention to coal production. It is estimated that the Northeast can produce 5 million tons next year, and one-fifth of it can be transported to Guannei. As soon as Huludao thaws next spring, it can begin. The Jiaozuo Coal Mine, which can produce 1,000 tons of white coal per day, has been recovered by the National Army and is actively producing. There are 140,000 tons of coal stored there. Unfortunately, the railway from Jiaozuo to Xinxiang has not been repaired, and the road is long, making it difficult to transport by train. We have now tried to negotiate with the United Nations Relief and Rehabilitation Administration (UNRRA) and will arrange for trucks to transport the coal from Xinxiang after it is transported from the production area.

Jiangya Steamer Repairs Boilers; Anshun Steamer Clears Allotment Fees

[Report from Our Newspaper] The Shanghai-Ningbo routes of the China Merchants Bureau are operated by the Jiangya and Jiangjing steamers. The Jiangya steamer is currently out of service for boiler repairs and is expected to be repaired within this week and resume service next week, so only the Jiangjing steamer travels between Shanghai and Ningbo. The Taikoo Steamship Company's Anshun steamer, on October 2, 1941 (that is, the 30th year of the Republic of China), loaded cargo and passengers from Shanghai and exported them, passing through Xiamen and Hong Kong to Singapore and Penang. A fire broke out en route, which was extinguished. The goods were slightly damaged, and the company entrusted Ruifang Foreign Firm to allocate water fees. At that time, various commercial firms paid a water fee guarantee of 20%. At that time, it happened that the Japanese invaders invaded the south, and the war was in full swing, so the progress was stopped. Now that victory has been achieved, in order to clear the procedures, the company has decided that from the 16th of this month, anyone holding a water fee guarantee receipt can register with Ruifen Foreign Firm until June 30th of next year. After the registration procedures are completed, the water fee method will be negotiated.

Exemption from Transportation Business Tax; Inland River Vessels Continue to Strive

Protagonist of the Scandalous Disappearance Case Before the August 13th Incident, Miyazaki Sadao, Appears in Japan After Ten Years of Imprisonment in China

[Special Report from Our Newspaper] Recent news from Japan indicates that a man named Miyazaki Sadao has reappeared.

Who is Miyazaki Sadao?

On July 24th, 1937, seventeen days after the July 7th Incident and nine days before August 13th, Shanghai was at its most tense. Suddenly, at ten o'clock that evening, two Japanese military officers reported to the Wayside Road Police Station that one private first class was missing during roll call of the Japanese Marine Corps that night. The private first class's name was Miyazaki Sadao.

While the Japanese military requested an investigation from the authorities, the Marine Corps immediately dispatched soldiers to patrol, cut off traffic, and inspect pedestrians, creating a very tense situation.

Yu Hongjun, then acting mayor of Shanghai, notified Japanese Consul General Okamoto, requesting him to act cautiously to avoid further agitating the public.

However, what was the Japanese side doing?

Major newspapers in Tokyo all reported the news with special headlines. Japanese warships sailed into the Wusongkou, led by the "Izumo" warship.

By the 26th, the situation had calmed down, and public sentiment gradually stabilized.

However, Miyazaki Sadao's whereabouts remained unknown.

The Japanese Consulate was still holding daily meetings in a state of panic, but suddenly, Miyazaki Sadao was found in the river off Bazhugang, Jingjiang County!

Below is an excerpt from Miyazaki's "confession" at the police station, with his fingerprint affixed at the end:

"At around nine o'clock on the afternoon of the 24th, I went alone to a brothel on Bazilu. At nine-thirty, I paid two dollars and wanted to walk back, but three people who seemed to be Chinese chased after me, demanding more money. After arguing for a while, I took a rickshaw towards the Peace Pagoda. However, when I came out of the brothel, a Japanese sailor saw me arguing with these three people. He saw me arguing with them, and because I was wearing a military uniform, I was afraid of being recognized, so I threw away my military cap and collar before taking the rickshaw to the Peace Pagoda. After passing the Peace Pagoda, I wrapped the uniform in a newspaper and hid for two nights. On the morning of the 26th, I boarded a British ship to escape. On the ship, I slept on the deck. The crew said they would report to the captain. Because I had no ticket, I was overcome with fear, so at one o'clock in the afternoon of the 26th, I jumped into the Yangtze River. By that time, the ship had already reached Jingjiang. On the 27th, I was rescued."

Jingjiang County sent him to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and on the afternoon of the 28th, the man was handed over to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs handed him back to the Japanese military authorities.

However, when he was in the hands of the Japanese military, they felt they had lost a great deal of face. The protagonist of this farce was immediately arrested, accused of the crime of encroaching and selling stolen goods, and sent back to his country, where he was imprisoned until recently.

Miyazaki Sadao spent ten years in prison. The Japanese military authorities seemed to think that they had covered up the shame.

This is the behavior of a "samurai" in a country that often boasts of its "Bushido"!

Two Missing Beloved Sons Wander in Public Office, Owner of Money Exchange Business Suffers Failure and Great Fright

[Report from Our Newspaper] Jiang Yaotang, a 40-year-old from Zhenjiang, opened the Xietai Money Exchange at No. 180 Nanjing Road and resided at No. 111 Zhaofeng Villa, Changning Road. He had a wife, Gu, and a concubine, Wu, who got along well with each other. Gu had two sons, the elder named Lingdi, nine years old, and the younger named Maomao, only four years old. The family lived happily together. Unexpectedly, the Xietai Exchange suffered excessive losses recently and closed down on the 9th. Rumors spread, and creditors went to Jiang's residence to demand repayment, carrying away redwood furniture as collateral. At that time, Jiang had no choice but to let them do as they pleased and voluntarily issued written guarantees promising to repay on a specific date. After the creditors left, Yaotang also went out shortly afterward. Before long, another group of creditors arrived, and while they were making a commotion, unexpectedly, Jiang's two children, Lingdi and Maomao, went missing at the same time. After Gu discovered this, she urgently reported it to the Changning Road Sub-Bureau, requesting an investigation. The police were dispatched to investigate in all directions, but they found no clues that night. By about eleven o'clock yesterday morning, the two children were suddenly found in French Park. The gardener reported it to the Lujiiawan Sub-Bureau, which sent police to bring them back. At the same time, the Changning Sub-Bureau was notified, ordering the police to go and bring them back for verification. According to the two children, two people took them into a car and drove away quickly. After spending the night, they did not know how, they were sent to French Park the next morning. This matter is quite suspicious. Whether it was a prank by an enemy or had other intentions, it has not been clarified yet.

Case of Section Chief of Executive Headquarters Embezzling Public Funds: Investigation Completed, Public Prosecution Initiated, Wu Suiren Charged with Embezzlement, Beijing Office States in Letter That Wu Seemed Prepared for Embezzlement

[Report from Our Newspaper] The case of Wu Suiren, a clerk in the Disbursement Section of the General Affairs Department of the Executive Headquarters, embezzling public funds for lending and earning interest has been investigated by Prosecutor Liu Yongzhi of the District Prosecutor's Office, and a public prosecution has been initiated on charges of embezzlement.

According to the charges, Wu Suiren took advantage of his position to embezzle 2.7 billion yuan of the Executive Headquarters' September expenses for lending and earning interest. On October 28th, when the headquarters discovered this, Wu expressed remorse and returned all 2.7 billion yuan of public funds along with the 14.6 million yuan in interest earned. Although the Executive Headquarters did not suffer any losses, the embezzlement of public funds violated criminal law. The Director of the Executive Headquarters, Huo Doushu, sent a letter to the District Prosecutor's Office on November 16th with the full details of the case, requesting legal action. After accepting the case, the office issued an arrest warrant and detained Wu Suiren on the morning of the 27th. The prosecution has been initiated after investigation.

Three Other Remittances Found to Be Suspicious

[Another Report] The Beijing office of the Executive Headquarters sent a letter to the headquarters in Shanghai stating that Wu Suiren seemed to be prepared for embezzlement. On August 16th, Wu sent a letter to the Beijing office requesting that the check be changed to a payee check for easy withdrawal. Therefore, in addition to the 2.7 billion yuan embezzlement case, there are also: (1) 1.8 billion yuan remitted from Beijing to Shanghai on September 13th to cover the UNRRA's August funds; (2) 200 million yuan remitted from Beijing to Shanghai on October 3rd to cover the UNRRA's August funds; (3) 500 million yuan remitted from Beijing to Shanghai on October 24th to cover the UNRRA's September additional allocation. All of these remittances were delayed, with the suspicion of earning interest.

A Folding Fan: Second Trial, Chen Mo Denies Concealment, Insists He Purchased It in Chengdu

[Report from Our Newspaper] Chen Mo (also known as Chen Bingsi), who was sued by the Sino-American Cooperative Organization for concealing a folding fan from the Qianlong period of the traitor Liang Hongzhi, had a hearing at the High Court yesterday afternoon. Chen's wife and witness Cai Depei were also summoned. After the hearing, the court adjourned for another hearing, and the defendant was remanded in custody.

First, Chen's wife was questioned. Chen's wife, wearing a black sea tiger velvet coat, red scarf, and yellow high-heeled leather shoes, said she was 28 years old. She claimed that she married Chen Mo in 1937 and moved into No. 45 Yuyuan Lane, Yuguo Road, last November. The sofa in the house was borrowed from Wan Molin, the mahogany tables and chairs were purchased from Cai Xingtai Woodware Store on Baishi Road, the four paintings by Wang Yiting were gifts from Qian Jingen, and the Qianlong-era folding fan was purchased around the tenth day of the first lunar month of 1944 at a painting and calligraphy stall outside the Wuhou Shrine in Chengdu, paying 6,000 yuan. Cai Depei can testify to this.

Request for Confrontation

Next, Chen Mo was questioned. Chen, wearing a coffee-colored camel wool robe and black leather shoes, nodded to his family as he entered the courtroom, standing in the defendant's dock with an arrogant expression. He stated that he was formerly the leader of the Advance Detachment of the Loyal and Righteous National Salvation Army and resigned around September 10th last year. He is now in the import and export business. In August of last year, because the Advance Army Detachment had no place to live, he moved into the residence of the traitor Li Tuqun through the introduction of Tang Shengming. He left the residence at the end of August when the unit was ordered to go to Liuhe for concentration. He was not there to seal it off. This can be verified by the wife of the traitor Li, Ye Jiqing. He does not know where the residence of the traitor Liang Hongzhi is. The residence of the traitor Chen Qun was occupied by the Military Statistics Bureau. He denied that the Qianlong-era folding fan belonged to Liang Hongzhi. His account of how he purchased the folding fan was the same as his wife's. The court presented two letters of accusation from the Sino-American Cooperative Organization for the defendant to read. Chen argued: He does not know the accuser Wu Yongqing and would prefer that he appear in court for confrontation. At this point, the court ordered Chen Mo to sit aside and then summoned the witness Cai Depei to testify.

Merchant Testifies

Cai Depei said: He used to study at West China Union University in Chengdu and is now a merchant in Shanghai. He met the defendant in Hong Kong in 1939. Around the first month of 1944, he accompanied Chen Mo and Chen's wife to Wuhou Shrine, and he saw him purchase a folding fan at a painting and calligraphy stall. One side was a landscape painting, and the other side was calligraphy. It had bamboo bones and was one foot long; it looked somewhat old.

At this point, the court announced that further investigation was needed, adjourned for another hearing, and stated that a request for bail could be made in a separate statement. The defendant was remanded in custody after meeting with his family.

The Bleak Hardware and Used Goods Industry Cannot Bear to Recall the Mantingfang, The Prosperous Era Has Become History

[Special Report from Our Newspaper] "Jinyuli" and "Mantingfang," these names are beautiful enough—beautiful to the point of being ironic. Walking into an archway-style gate, you enter a dirty and dark alley. Following the damp cobblestone road, you turn west and pass through a dark teahouse. "Jinyuli" ends, followed by "Mantingfang," not a garden full of fragrant flowers, but some dim, rusty brass and white iron. Although this place is called "fang" (neighborhood), it is actually a narrow street, reaching Shilou to the west and Xishanglin Street to the east. In this short street, shops are set up, displaying many stalls of scrap copper and old iron. These stalls are similar to the loads carried by small coppersmiths, but larger in area. From east to west, there are more than twenty large ones. Some people, because they have no business, may rest for two days or even a day.

History of Stalls Over Forty Years

The place has a historical origin. According to the stall vendors, stalls have been set up here as early as forty years ago. At first, it was incense and hardware, but slowly the incense industry declined, while the hardware industry became more and more prosperous, from few to many, from small to prominent. Some have gone from stall vendors to shop owners; some have expanded from small stalls to large stalls; some have changed from helpers to self-employed; some have flown high and far away and become giants in the hardware industry. In short, the people here have passed on from father to son, from master to apprentice, and after forty years of the rise and fall of the times, the name "Mantingfang" has been established. The stall vendor stretched his hand out of his sleeve and pointed to a hardware store opposite, saying, "That store was originally a stall vendor, but later it changed into a store." I looked at the store. The storefront was small, and the wares were messy, but compared to the stalls, it was outstanding. The store owner might feel proud. After years of hard work, he has finally acquired this family business, although this business, as it looks now, is still inevitably depressed and declining.

Odds and Ends, Many Varieties

The goods here are mostly odds and ends, such as huge steel pliers, small copper locks, hammers, drills, iron rods, files, etc... There are also machine parts, vehicle materials, etc. Because they are messy and miscellaneous, it is most suitable to sell them by stall vendors. People with vision may want to come and rummage around. A discarded machine may find an inexpensive part here to be reused; a broken car may get what it needs here and run again. But these are all things of the past. Now this place has become very deserted. The stall vendor said to me, "You have been here for half a day, have you seen a single stall do business?" Indeed, not only has no business been done, but even people who inquire have not appeared. Even if someone buys a small part, it is a drop in the bucket for them. Their hope is to clear all the goods together and change to another industry. They are not satisfied with occasionally selling one or two items. Perhaps they are happier when reporters come to talk to them, so they can use this opportunity to complain!

Victory Arrives, Inventory Devalues

From 1944, during the period when the enemy plundered scrap iron, it seemed to be their prosperous period. Their goods were not subject to the plunder, and things were scarce and expensive. They really made a small fortune at that time. But after the victory, the puppet currency was valued at 200 to 1, and the inventory devalued, and business immediately declined!

Number of Opium and Drug Offenders Arrested Last Month Reached 220

The Committee for the Eradication of Opium and Drugs has scheduled the start of the Anti-Opium and Drug Propaganda Week on the 16th of this month. According to statistics released yesterday by the Police Bureau Statistical Office: a total of 220 opium and drug offenders were arrested last month, which can be further divided into two categories: addicts and traffickers. The former category included 117 males and 55 females. In terms of age, the largest number was in the 41-45 age group, totaling 44 people. The next largest groups were the 31-35 and 51-55 age groups, with 27 and 26 people respectively. Following that were the elderly over 56, totaling 18 people. Those aged 36-40 and 46-50 each numbered 16. Young people under 30 totaled 25. In terms of occupation, the unemployed accounted for the largest number, totaling 55 people, followed by those in commerce, totaling 53, and those in domestic service, totaling 35. These three categories accounted for 83% of the total. As for drug traffickers, 34 males and 14 females were arrested. The majority of these offenders were also unemployed or engaged in commerce, with the former accounting for 22 and the latter for 15, totaling 77% of the total. In terms of the areas where opium and drug offenders were arrested, the Taishan District had the highest number, totaling 44 people, followed by the Laozha District, totaling 22. Next was the Yimiao District, with 19 people. The Xincheng District had 15, and the Jiangning, Tilanqiao, and Yangjing districts each had 13. In addition, there were ten major districts, including Jing'an Temple and North Railway Station, where the Bureau headquarters arrested a total of 81 people.

Reader Consultation: Medicine and Health

(1) Peeling Hands

Asked by Xu Wenkui

I suffer from a skin disease on my hands. The palms are red and peeling, and one joint on my fingers cannot be straightened. Where the skin is not peeling, it is firm, thick, and rough. I don't know if it's dyshidrotic eczema, and how should I treat it?

[Answer by Dr. Zhang Zhongming] Your condition is likely dyshidrotic eczema, but there are many types of skin diseases. It is advisable to consult a doctor for diagnosis and medication.

(2) Many Illnesses for Postpartum Woman

Wei Jifu asks: Two months after childbirth, a woman suddenly suffered from swollen feet. A hard, movable lump appeared on the side of her neck, and it is gradually increasing in size. The local doctor said it was scrofula, and repeated treatments have not been effective. Recently, another lump has grown elsewhere. Please answer: (1) What is this disease? What is the cause? (2) The woman has not had her period for nine months. Is this related to the illness? (3) What kind of doctor should she consult for this condition? (4) The woman has been suffering from this for a long time, and her body is weak and emaciated. Can she take tonics? What is suitable? (5) The child is nine months old, and the fontanelle on the top of the head has not yet closed. Is this a congenital deficiency? Is it beneficial to take calcium, Haliver oil drops, and milk powder? (6) If the child drinks the milk from the mother with the hard lump on her neck, will it harm the child's health?

[Answer by Dr. Zhang Zhongming] (1) This hard object is a swollen lymph node. The causes can be tuberculous, syphilitic, and pyogenic, among others. (2) During breastfeeding, a woman's period may be temporarily suspended. (3) All public hospitals in Shanghai can treat this, and the fees are relatively low. (4) If the woman is weak, she can take cod liver oil and various other tonics. (5) The anterior fontanelle of a child usually closes around one year of age. Your child is only nine months old and the anterior fontanelle has not yet closed, so it cannot be called a congenital deficiency. Calcium, vitamins, and milk powder complement each other and are very good, but avoid excessive amounts. (6) If the hard object the woman has is infectious, it can infect the child.
