Completely Eliminate the Black Market for Cotton Yarn: Concrete Plan Principles Have Been Established; Government Provides Foreign Exchange but Requires Cotton to be Exchanged for Cotton Yarn; Cotton Spinning Association Discusses Implementation Plan Today

[Our Dispatch] In order to completely eliminate the black market for cotton yarn, Premier Song summoned Wu, the concurrent chairman of the Cotton Management Committee, Wang Qiyu, Wu Weijing, Rong Hongyuan, and Rong Yixin again yesterday morning at 10:00 AM to discuss concrete plans. It is rumored that the basic principles have been generally determined, and the main points are as follows: (1) Raw materials: (A) A small committee for reviewing the allocation of raw cotton will be established, with Li Yu, director of the Allocation Department of the Executive Committee of the Women's Management Committee, and one representative each from national and private yarn factories serving as members. (B) Within the limit of permitted raw cotton imports, each yarn factory will be allowed to allocate it themselves. (2) Finished products: In principle, it is stipulated that cotton yarn be exchanged for cotton. In other words, the government will provide foreign exchange for purchasing cotton and simultaneously recover a portion of the cotton yarn at a negotiated price. Any surplus will still be freely bought and sold by each yarn factory. (3) The operations of national and private yarn factories will be unified. In addition to the Spinning and Construction Company, which has already resumed the listed system, the opening of yarn by private factories should be handled centrally by the Sixth District Cotton Spinning Association. The association will still organize an allocation and sales committee to open yarn by listing prices. (4) Before each opening of yarn, the standard price for each type of yarn should be negotiated based on its quality and type, under the principle of being lower than the market price. The pricing should be flexible and can be adjusted according to market needs and the factory's own yarn inventory.

The Sixth District Cotton Spinning Association, following Premier Song's instructions, convened a meeting of executive directors yesterday morning at 11:00 AM. Wang Qiyu, Wu Weijing, Rong Hongyuan, Tang Xinghai, Liu Jingji, Guo Qiong, and others attended. The principles decided at the meeting summoned by Premier Song were made into a plan, which will be submitted to the regular meeting of the Cotton Management Committee at 3:00 PM on the 12th for discussion. At the same time, detailed implementation rules will be studied.

According to a person involved, the government's opening of foreign exchange settlement for American cotton imports will be handled in quarterly installments (i.e., three months). Based on the current production volume of cotton yarn in China, the permitted import limit for each quarter is estimated to be approximately 200,000 to 300,000 bales. At that time, in order to promote domestic cotton, the government will match a certain proportion of domestic cotton based on the amount of American cotton applied for purchase. It is also observed that if the cotton-yarn exchange system is implemented, the government will be able to supply the textile industry with the large amount of raw cotton it needs, and the government will also be able to easily obtain a large amount of cotton yarn. Although there will still be a surplus for factories to buy and sell freely, it will be a small portion. Therefore, it is expected that the future trend of yarn prices will undoubtedly be stable. At the same time, in the future, the opening of yarn will be listed, and national and private yarn factories will take the same steps. Pricing will also be flexible, so it is expected that the black market for cotton yarn can be eradicated as a result.

Flour Mills Struggle to Survive Due to Raw Material Shortages and Price Limits Below Cost

The flour milling industry in this city is second only to the cotton textile industry. Flour mills throughout the city have 4,800 large mills, 102 small mills, 114 motors, and 10,200 horsepower. Currently, due to electricity restrictions, production has been greatly reduced. According to industry leaders, the industry's production is limited on one hand by electricity restrictions, preventing full operation, and on the other hand by raw material restrictions. The amount of wheat needed for flour is insufficient in China and relies heavily on foreign imports. In recent months, various countries have restricted exports, so the source of supply has become an increasing problem. If there are no more foreign wheat imports in the future, some factories may have to stop production next year. In addition, the manufacturing cost of the industry is very high, and the price limits are low, making it difficult for factories to maintain operations.

Supplementary Measures for Foreign Businesses Operating in Shanghai Have Been Formulated

[Our Dispatch] Supplementary measures have been formulated for the regulations governing the operation of foreign businesses in this city. The required documents are as follows: (1) Commercial registration application form. (2) Nationality certificate of the person concerned or the agent. (3) If the business is a partnership, the original or a copy of the partnership agreement and the names and addresses of the partners. (4) If the head office is located in this country or in other commercial ports or this city within China, and the registration is for the establishment of a branch, the original or a copy of the commercial registration certificate of the head office. (5) If a manager or agent is appointed, the name, nationality, address, and proof of authority must be stated in the application form. If the manager is a foreigner, a nationality certificate must be added. (6) If approval from the competent authority is required by laws and regulations, the approval document must be added. (7) Foreign business operation investigation form.

Silk Weaving Industry Requests Loans Totaling 66 Billion Yuan; Each Loom to be Mortgaged for 12 Billion Yuan; Request Being Submitted to Government Authorities for Assistance

[Our Dispatch] The electric silk weaving industry in this city, facing difficult circumstances, has submitted documents to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Economic Affairs, and the Joint Treasury, requesting the government to provide assistance in terms of loans and orders. Regarding the loan measures, the industry's specific requests are as follows:

I. Relax the loan amount and mortgage measures as follows:

A. The total loan amount is 66 billion yuan, with a loan of 12 million yuan per loom (estimated total number of looms is 5,500).

B. Each loom and equipment is mortgaged for 6 million yuan, semi-finished products on the loom are mortgaged for 4 million yuan, and finished woven products are mortgaged for 2 million yuan, totaling the above amount (if there are no semi-finished products on the loom or the number of finished woven products is insufficient, the amount will be deducted based on the actual amount).

C. Use of the loan

(1) Repay old debts and high-interest loans

(2) Purchase raw materials

(3) Pay wages and other expenses

The above three items shall not be used for other purposes

D. The interest rate shall be 2.2% per month, following the precedent of silk cocoon loans.

II. Accept orders from state-owned agencies, following the same industry practice of releasing materials for subcontracted weaving. State-owned agencies will issue raw materials and customize silk loans that meet export standards. Detailed methods will be stipulated separately in the contract.

Regarding orders, the industry association suggested that the factory silk stored by the China Trust Bureau be processed by the industry's factories and transported to Southeast Asia, the United States, Canada, and other places to open up overseas markets. The petition also pointed out that the China Trust Bureau's price for each carton of rayon is 2.8 million yuan, while the price of the government's barter trade with Japan is only 500,000 yuan per carton according to the Hong Kong market price, and the profit amount is more than 2 million yuan per carton. As of now, the factories that have purchased the products include 5,400 cartons from the Property Management Office and 4,300 cartons from the China Trust Bureau, for a total government profit of 20 billion yuan. Therefore, if national banks and bureaus can release funds at this time, it would truly be "taking from the same industry and using it for the same industry." Finally, it was expressed that if the request is not approved, the factories have no other choice but to close down and transfer all factory properties, machinery, and more than 20,000 workers and staff to the state for proper disposition.

Saving the Industrial and Commercial Crisis: Actively Handling Production Loans; Regulations for the Production Loan Review Committee Drafted

Yesterday morning (the 10th), Premier Song convened a meeting with key figures from the financial, industrial, and commercial sectors of the city to discuss resolving the current economic crisis. He first announced that measures had been approved to assist legitimate production enterprises with funding. He urged national financial institutions and commercial firms to actively provide loans based on the actual needs of each industry. A temporary review committee for production enterprise loans would be established by the Four Banks Joint Treasury to oversee the process. It is understood that the committee has already begun work. The Four Banks Joint Treasury has appointed Huo Shishu, Li Fusun, Qin Runqing, Xu Jiguan, Gu Chunfan, Ouyang Lun, Lin Fengbao, Cai Gongchun, Zhao Dihua, Li Shuming, Liu Gongyun, and Xu Guangchi as committee members, with Huo Shishu designated as the chairman and Li Fusun, Xu Jiguan, Gu Chunfan, and Lin Fengbao as standing committee members. The first meeting was held yesterday at 5 PM to discuss implementation methods. The draft regulations for the committee are outlined below:

(1) The Four Banks Joint Treasury establishes the Temporary Review Committee for Production Enterprise Loans to support production enterprises in line with government policy.

(2) The committee members are appointed by the Four Banks Joint Treasury from the following personnel:

A. Heads of relevant banks and bureaus

B. Heads of relevant agencies

C. Responsible personnel from the Chamber of Commerce and the Silver and Banking Guild

(3) The committee consists of one chairman and four standing committee members, designated by the Four Banks Joint Treasury from among the committee members.

(4) The committee meets at least three times a week to review cases submitted by the Four Banks Joint Treasury, the Four Banks branches, banking syndicates, or commercial firms. The chairman may convene ad hoc meetings when necessary. The chairman may invite relevant personnel to attend committee meetings.

(5) The handling of each case, except for those that the committee resolves to submit to the Four Banks Joint Treasury for approval, may be directly delegated to the respective banks for handling, with a subsequent report for record.

(6) The banks handling loan applications should expedite the process in accordance with the regulations for handling loan applications of the Four Banks Joint Treasury.

(7) The Central Bank should provide refinancing against the loans granted by the banks under the approved terms.

(8) The Four Banks Joint Treasury, the Central, Communications, and Agricultural Banks, the Central Trust Bureau, the Joint Credit Information Center, the Silver and Banking Guild, and relevant government agencies should provide the committee with as much information and assistance as possible regarding the investigation, evaluation, supervision, and assistance of production enterprises.

(9) The committee should supervise the banks' monitoring of the business and financial conditions of the production enterprises that have received loans. If improper use of loans or failure to meet planned production targets is discovered, the committee should urge improvement or recover the loan and report to the committee.

(10) The committee has a secretary and several staff members, seconded from the various banks of the Four Banks Joint Treasury.

The daily affairs of the committee in Shanghai shall be handled concurrently by the Shanghai branch of the Four Banks Joint Treasury.

(11) These regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the board of directors of the Four Banks Joint Treasury and may be amended in the same manner.

National Assembly Education Representatives Hu Shi and Others Submit Recommendations, Requesting the Government to Pay Attention to Educational Issues

[Our Nanjing Dispatch] National Assembly representatives from the free professional education sector, including Hu Shi, Cao Chu, Ye Suzhong, Ge Wei, Yang Zhan, Huang Zhaoxiong, Chen Bai, Zhou Feicheng, Jiang Jianbai, Zhou Houxu, Wang Ziyu, Wang Yizhou, Gu Tonghe, Zhu Jingnong, Chen Xifang, Liang Xinda, Zhang Yi, and Ruan Zhidato, submitted a proposal to the National Assembly requesting the government to pay attention to the major issues currently affecting education. The original proposal is excerpted below: Education is the foundation of a nation and the basis for implementing democratic politics. As the Constitution is being drafted and the government is about to return power to the people, the widespread promotion of education is particularly essential to enable the people to have the capacity to implement the Constitution and exercise political power. In addition to the Constitution containing comprehensive and adaptable provisions for education to ensure that the nation's basic policies can be implemented without hindrance, we must express our views on important current educational matters for the government to consider in its educational arrangements and to encourage those in society who care about education to sympathize, unanimously advocate, and promote their realization.

Employ Specialists to Improve Efficiency

First, the government should employ specialists to manage education. Education in modern times has become a specialized discipline, and educational undertakings in general society are even more specialized. Therefore, those who manage education must have specialized knowledge and experience. Currently, those engaged in educational administration and teaching lack knowledge and experience. Many people still believe that anyone can manage educational administration and educational undertakings, and that anyone can be a teacher. Therefore, various unqualified individuals advance, and achievements are not remarkable, and education is not taken seriously. These errors must be corrected immediately. The government must carefully appoint educational administrative personnel at all levels. Educational authorities must pay attention to employing specialists related to the education being provided. Middle and primary school teachers should be filled by those who have received normal school training, so that educational efficiency can be improved, and the mission of education can be gradually achieved.

Allocate Enemy and Puppet Assets to Funding

Second, the government should allocate huge sums of money to actively manage education. During the Anti-Japanese War, education and culture suffered the most damage. Since the victory, the restoration of education and culture has been the slowest. Society has failed to provide widespread assistance, and the government has failed to do its utmost. Within the entire economic system, some people only see the consumption of education and forget the contribution of education to the future of the nation. As a result, many destroyed schools cannot be restored, and schools that should be added cannot be built. Countless children and young people are roaming the streets without schools to attend, and the situation is extremely serious. The central government should have a long-term vision and regard the restoration of education and the addition of schools as an unavoidable responsibility. It should allocate huge sums of money to subsidize the restoration of public and private schools at all levels and to add new schools to accommodate out-of-school children and young people in order to reverse the current downward trend. In addition, enemy, puppet, and traitor assets in various localities should be allocated to educational funding, because enemy and puppet assets mostly come from the exploitation of the people, and using them for education best meets the people's wishes.

Restore County Education Bureaus Early

Third, the government should restore county education bureaus and provide substantial subsidies for local education as early as possible. Local education below the county level has been disrupted by the destruction of the enemy and puppets and the impact of the centralized collection and expenditure of fiscal funds. The promotion of universal education has also been delayed, and the original independent spirit of educational funding has been completely destroyed and diverted for other uses in large quantities. For example, local educational funding before the war accounted for 40% or 50% or more, but now it has dropped to about 10%. The original educational funding was not abundant. Looking at the current situation of local education, school facilities are simple and insufficient for teaching, teachers' salaries are low, with monthly incomes of 40,000 to 50,000 yuan, which cannot even maintain their personal lives. Excellent teachers have switched to other professions, and unqualified personnel account for more than 300,000 of the 600,000 teachers. There are even more than 80,000 primary school graduates who serve as primary school teachers. The seriousness of the situation is self-evident. In the future, on the one hand, provinces should be ordered to restore county education bureaus in 1947, and on the other hand, the system of guaranteeing local educational funding should be restored, and funds must be used for specific purposes. On the one hand, the central government should increase subsidies for local national education funding, at least bearing one-quarter, in order to achieve universal education as soon as possible.

Reward and Subsidize Private Schools

Fourth, the government should vigorously support and subsidize private education. Currently, private schools account for more than one-third of the number of schools in our country, which shows that private education greatly benefits the national education cause. Since the victory, the government has ignored private education. Some excellent private schools are unable to rebuild, and the government has not provided effective financial assistance. This is a major defect in education. Private school teachers and staff are also national public educators, but they do not enjoy the same treatment as the state. We hope that the government will attach equal importance to educational undertakings, regardless of public or private, and provide rewards and subsidies to private schools and equal treatment to private school teachers. As for private schools that were destroyed during the Anti-Japanese War and still want to restore their schools, we hope that the government will provide effective financial assistance.

Raise Teachers' Salaries Immediately

Fifth, the government should raise teachers' salaries. Educational personnel, whether engaged in national education or other levels of education, hold the key to the nation's new life. Recently, due to high prices and difficult living conditions, teachers at all levels are feeling pain, especially primary school teachers. How can educational efficiency be achieved if teachers cannot be fed and clothed? Currently, the transfer and retreat of teachers at all levels has become a common phenomenon. If active rescue is not taken, it may cause extremely serious consequences. It is hoped that the government will have the greatest determination and make the greatest decision to immediately raise teachers' salaries so that they can meet the actual needs of local life and increase them with the increase in the cost of living so that they can work with peace of mind and specialize.

Strictly Order the Return of Occupied School Buildings

Sixth, the government should strictly supervise and order the return of school buildings and other buildings occupied by defendants. At the beginning of the victory, the order was unsettled, and many troops and administrative organs occupied the houses of schools and cultural institutions. When the order was restored, education should be restored at the same time, but the occupied school buildings and other buildings are often not returned for a long time. As for ten schools, they cannot be restored early. Although the government has issued a notice, it has not been thoroughly implemented. I hope the government will strictly order its subordinates to seriously handle it and return it immediately, so that the education community will not develop resentment.

French Claim My Cultural and Educational Contributions Are Great

[French News Agency, Paris, November 11] A reception was held here last night by Chinese and French figures. Ministry of Education Promulgates Regulations for Substitute National Schools; Municipal Education Bureau Ordered to Comply

In order to promote national education, the Ministry of Education has promulgated regulations for substitute national schools and ordered the education bureaus of various provinces and cities to comply. After receiving this instruction, the municipal education bureau will formulate specific measures to follow and implement. The Ministry's order promulgating the regulations for substitute national schools is excerpted below: (Article 1) These regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 6, Paragraph 2 of the National School Law. (Article 2) In counties and cities where national schools have not yet been widely established, private primary schools with excellent performance, verified by county and city supervisors, and with the consent of the private primary school board of directors, shall be designated as substitute national schools, referred to as Substitute National School of Mou County (City), Mou Township, Mou Mou Bao. (Article 3) Substitute national schools are subordinate to the county (city) government or the education administrative organs directly under the jurisdiction of the municipality, and are subject to the management, supervision, and guidance of the competent authorities. However, the original board of directors of the school may still provide opinions, which shall be adopted and implemented by the competent authorities. (Article 4) After a private primary school is converted into a national school, its expenses shall be borne by the county (city) government or the municipal education administrative organs. However, the original property of the private primary school shall still be managed by the board of directors of the private primary school for the purpose of enriching school equipment, etc., and shall not be nationalized. (Article 5) After a private primary school is converted into a substitute national school, its principal shall be appointed by the county (city) government upon recommendation by the school board. Teachers shall still be hired by the principal. The original principal and teachers shall not be removed unless they are unqualified or there are circumstances specified in Article 12 of the National School Teachers and Staff Appointment and Treatment Protection Measures. (Article 6) Substitute national schools shall be divided into basic education, with four semesters of one to four years as a principle. When necessary, advanced (fifth and sixth grade) out-of-school public remedial education may also be established, with primary adult classes and women's classes as a principle. When necessary, advanced adult classes and women's classes may also be established. (Article 7) The curriculum, teaching materials, equipment, teachers and staff, and all other facilities of substitute national schools shall be handled in accordance with the rules of national schools and central national schools. (Article 8) After a private primary school is converted into a substitute national school, if the competent educational administrative organ intends to revoke its substitute status, or the board of directors of the private primary school requests to restore its private nature, it may restore its private nature after both parties agree. (Article 9) After a private school is converted into a substitute national school, if the original board of directors of the private primary school is unwilling to continue to operate and is willing to donate all the school's property to the public, its substitute nature may be revoked and it may be converted into a national school. (Article 10) These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Taken by Special Correspondent Shao Shenzhi of This Newspaper

Double Twelfth Today's Xi'an

Wuxi Industry Marches Forward Against the Headwinds of Economic Downturn

— Our Reporter Ding Weidong

Three Pillars: Cotton Mills, Flour Mills, Silk Mills

The degree of industrialization in Wuxi is second only to Shanghai on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway line. The number of industrial electricity consumption is sufficient to prove this fact. The power plant at Qi Qiao delivers 8,000 horsepower of power to Wuxi industry every day, which is not a small amount, but the shortage of electricity is still a problem. Large industries barely have enough power, and many small industries that sprang up during the war have to install their own power generation equipment at considerable cost. According to the engineers of the power plant, to meet all the needs of Wuxi industry, it would probably be necessary to increase the power by another 8,000 horsepower per day! And this is only the current situation. With the current high profits of cotton mills and the diligence and pragmatism of the people of Wuxi, there are quite a few people who are making expansion plans. Those who ordered spindles from overseas will continue to return in the next year or two. As productivity expands, the need for electricity will become even more urgent. If we use this as a measure, we can see that the future of Wuxi's industrialization is truly limitless!

There are three pillars of Wuxi industry: cotton mills, flour mills, and silk mills. Due to objective environmental factors, the prosperity and decline of these three industries are very different today. During my brief trip, I had contact with people from all three industries and gained a general understanding of the difficulties and prospects of each industry. Now, I will try to provide a comprehensive report in the order of cotton, flour, and silk.

Lucky Cotton Industry: Profitable as Long as Management is Sound

The cotton spinning industry is undoubtedly the darling of heaven among China's troubled industries today. Demand is high while production is insufficient, the black market price is high, and raw materials are relatively cheap. Whether it is a large factory or a small factory, as long as the management is sound, there is no way not to make a lot of money. The price of cotton yarn in Wuxi is not limited, and the selling price is around 2.3 million yuan per bale. The prosperity of the yarn weaving industry can be imagined. As for the cotton mills in Wuxi, the larger ones with higher output include Shenxin No. 3 Factory and others. Please refer to the attached table below:

There are more than a dozen other small cotton mills with one or two thousand spindles. The above table lists the highest number of equipment in each factory. In fact, much was destroyed during the war, and some are still in the process of being repaired. Not so many are operating today. How many spindles are spinning in Wuxi today? There are two estimates: one is about 100,000 spindles, and the other is about 110,000 spindles. This means that the current yarn production is only about 60% of what it was before the war. At the beginning of the Anti-Japanese War, when the enemy occupied Wuxi, they deeply hated the Chinese textile industry, which hindered the national policy of "Industrial Japan, Agricultural China." 70,000 spindles of Shenxin No. 3 Factory were systematically destroyed, leaving only 10,000 spindles! As for the 1478 looms, they were completely destroyed. Shenxin's experience was like this, and the fate of other major factories was similar. But today, one year after the victory of the Anti-Japanese War, although the country is in trouble and the social economy is turbulent, I have been able to witness Shenxin being able to restore 50,000 spindles, and the weaving factory has begun to equip itself in the burnt-out factory building. It is possible that 500 looms will be running in December. Workers and staff are working with the same enthusiasm under the brilliant electric lights; other factories also have prospects and expectations for tomorrow. The past experience seems to be just a nightmare, and everything has disappeared with the victory. I deeply feel that the Chinese people's resilience and vitality are the strongest reliance on overcoming all difficulties. The raw materials for Wuxi yarn mills are mainly American cotton, and occasionally some Brazilian cotton. Before the war, they were able to produce fine yarns of 40s and 60s counts, but now the machinery is damaged, and they can only spin coarse yarns of 20s and 30s counts. The treatment of workers is also better than in other industries, generally ranging from 80,000 to 320,000, and the treatment of technical foremen can also reach 500,000 to 600,000 yuan. Their wages are calculated according to the cost of living. According to a friend in the factory, it is about 80% of the wages in Shanghai. Labor disputes in Wuxi are far less common than in Shanghai. There are two reasons: most of the major technicians in major yarn mills have been serving for many years, sharing hardships together. Over time, they gradually develop feelings. Even if there are any requests, they are made in a spirit of friendly consultation, and rarely appear in the form of strikes. Second, Wuxi is not like Shanghai. The local situation is simpler, and there is no large-scale organization or manipulation of workers, so the situation is more stable. Recently, Wuxi workers, in view of the high cost of living, have demanded that the base salary be increased by half. The management will take a rejecting attitude on this matter, so it is difficult to predict whether the labor-management relationship can be as it was in the past. As for the efficiency of technicians, one factory owner said that it is only 70% to 80% of what it was before the war. It is not physical weakness, but psychological changes. Technicians feel that they are welcomed everywhere, and "if you don't keep me here, I can find a place elsewhere." Therefore, discipline is lost, and efficiency is reduced. I usually feel deeply that, in terms of the current industrial situation in our country, except for the abnormally prosperous cotton spinning industry, the burden of wages will suffocate national industry. But today it is impossible to reduce wages. Therefore, the only remedy is how to improve workers' sense of responsibility and enable them to spontaneously improve work efficiency.

Gloomy Flour Industry

Compared to the cotton yarn industry, flour mills and silk mills seem dim and lackluster. The latter is even in a crisis of raw material shortages. Before the war, flour was the main industry in Wuxi. The famous Rong family started their business with flour. The stone mill they used when they started their business is still on display as a family heirloom. During the nine years of the Anti-Japanese War, Wuxi experienced a distorted prosperity due to the enemy and puppet control of food. At that time, there were many people who raised funds to open flour mills. Today, the flour factories with scale in the area should be Maoxin, Guangfeng, and Zhenhua factories, etc. There are more than ten others that are smaller in scale. The current recession is mainly due to three reasons: (1) Insufficient power supply makes it impossible to fully exert productivity, but expenses cannot be saved. According to an estimate by a gentleman in this industry: The current daily output of flour in Wuxi is only 10,000 bags, but if there is enough electricity, it can be increased to 25,000 bags. This statement is quite reliable. In Maoxin No. 2 Factory, 8,000 bags of flour could be produced daily before the war, but now the output has been sharply reduced due to lack of electricity. 5,000 bags are produced on the first day, and 2,500 bags are produced on the second day, and so on. The situation in other factories is similar. (2) The supply of raw materials used to come mostly from northern Jiangsu, but due to the occupation by the Communist army, the supply is not smooth, which affects production. (3) The current general recession in the food industry, and the flour industry is no exception; the result is that the price of raw materials rises, while the selling price of flour does not rise, so there is no profit to be made. Under the above three unfavorable conditions, the current production of the flour industry is only 30% to 40% of what it was before the war. At the same time, the burden of taxation also shrinks the industry. Now, every bag of flour is subject to a goods tax of 400 yuan, and at the end of the year, there is also income tax and profit tax. A flour mill owner told the reporter that the monthly tax expenditure is much larger than the salaries and food expenses of the employees. Under the current situation of sluggish sales, small factories are deeply affected by high-interest loans, and one or two may announce liquidation at the end of the year.

Silk Industry Crisis: Even More Serious Than Flour Mills

The crisis in Wuxi's silk industry is even more serious than that of flour mills. Before the war, there were 40 silk factories in the area. During the nine years of the Anti-Japanese War, more than 20 small factories were established, for a total of more than 60 factories, employing more than 20,000 workers. The ones with more equipment are shown in the table below:

Factory Name Number of Machines

Bada 156

China Silk Factory No. 6 304

Zhengmao 104

Yongchang 114

Jincheng 272

Meixin 296

Yongtai 312

Dingxin 256

Jiangnan First Silk Reeling Factory 360

All of these silk factories, large and small, are currently in a raw material panic. If the shipment of silkworm cocoons to China cannot become a reality, then all of them will stop work before the end of this month. When the autumn silk comes on the market next year, the cost will become a most serious problem. The current government purchase price is 3.8 million yuan per picul (standard silk), but the cost of autumn silk is estimated to be more than 6 million yuan per picul. They are generally grateful for the government's good intentions to support the silk industry, and hope that the purchase price in the future can be adjusted according to the actual cost. As for the problem of raw silk exports, they have a common view: that our silk production has two major weaknesses: first, the silkworm varieties are not as good as others, so the quality of the silk is also poor; and second, wages are too high, so the production cost of silk is also high. In the short term, it is still difficult for us to compete with the strong enemy Japan.

A Productive City [More People Producing, Fewer People Consuming]

The current situation and prospects of Wuxi's three major industries have been briefly described above. Compared with other places, it brings hope. The same is true for industry and commerce. Of course, Wuxi's commerce is also in a recession, and there are also bankruptcies. On the day the reporter arrived in Wuxi, a large pharmacy was forced to close down by high-interest loans, and a rice store with more than ten years of history was struggling with a debt of 700 million yuan. The situation is miserable enough. However, the people of Wuxi who have money use their money to run businesses, instead of seeking high-interest loans and enjoying themselves, which has a very good impact. Because once a business is established, it employs a lot of people itself, and other industries also increase prosperity due to the so-called "multiplier effect" in economics. Therefore, the situation of unemployment in Wuxi is better than in other places. At the same time, because it is a productive place, the people's purchasing power is stronger, so even in the headwinds of the commercial recession, the market situation is still good. As for the lives of Wuxi farmers, they are not as good as they used to be. In the past, they had two sources of income every year, one was rice and the other was sericulture, and their lives were not bad. Since one year ago, they have been cutting mulberry trees and planting rice, but who knows that the rise in rice prices cannot be proportional to other prices! The hard work of farmers for a year cannot even make one or two sets of clothes. The big contradiction in our country's economy now is: if the price of rice is raised, the price of labor will definitely rise, and factories will not be able to maintain themselves; on the other hand, if the price of rice is not raised, then the lives of 80% of farmers will inevitably decline, and their purchasing power will be weak, and commerce will not be able to prosper. I asked this question to a friend in a Wuxi yarn mill. His opinion was: "In the past, the government tried to stabilize prices, but neglected labor prices. In the future, they should try to reduce labor prices in order to solve the problem."

Wuxi is a productive city, and there are very few idle people. There are "more people producing and fewer people consuming," so not only can it be self-sufficient, but it also has surplus material resources to export. The reason why it can be like this is because the natural environment is one reason, but the main reason is still human effort. The people's frugality and pragmatism, focusing on utilizing resources and improving people's lives, have finally turned Wuxi into a "Little Shanghai" - a productive city with the advantages of Shanghai but without the disadvantages of Shanghai. If three-tenths of the cities in China can concentrate the intelligence and wisdom of the people and develop into productive undertakings like the people of Wuxi, the reporter believes that the goal of improving people's lives can be realized sooner.

Enterprising Spirit: Repair Wartime Wounds, Strive to Expand Business

The industrial community in Wuxi has a very strong enterprising spirit. Their greatest advantage is that they live frugally, do not engage in extravagance, and use all their talents to develop their businesses. Now, most factories have development plans. They not only want to repair the wartime wounds, but also strive to expand their businesses. Taking the yarn industry as an example, both large and small factories are placing orders overseas. For example, Shenxin Yarn Factory had 70,000 spindles before the war. It suffered heavy losses during the war and has now only recovered to 50,000 spindles. However, they are now planning to increase to 126,000 spindles! On the eve of the end of the war, they placed orders with American manufacturers, and it is estimated that a part of them will be shipped next spring. The other yarn mills ordered later, and there are currently only three factories in the United States that can manufacture spinning machines, and their own needs are also great. Therefore, the production of Wuxi yarn mills will not increase much within a year. Taking flour mills as an example, the temporary recession is not enough to make the enterprising industrialists feel discouraged. On the contrary, they have also set ambitious development plans. For example, Maoxin No. 2 Factory is planning to purchase machinery to establish a large factory in Wuxi that produces 10,000 bags of flour per day. At the same time, Maoxin No. 1 Factory is also adding new British-made flour milling machines that were used during the war. The product performance is particularly good. All of this shows their enterprising spirit.

Power Problems

Insufficient power has restricted industrial production in the Wuxi area, and this problem is being smoothly resolved. There are various reasons for the power shortage in Wuxi. Firstly, many small industries have emerged in the past decade, and they all require electricity. Secondly, before the war, major factories had their own generators. However, during these turbulent years, some generators were lost, and some were left unused. This extra electricity burden affected the overall balance of supply and demand. As for the Qishuyan Power Plant's power supply, it has not decreased at all because the machinery was undamaged during the war. The Shenxin Textile Mill's generator is currently being borrowed by the power company to supply Wuxi. But this is still not enough. Many small factories cannot get electricity and have to generate their own power. Large factories also have limited electricity consumption; when exceeding the limit, they must supply coal to the Qishuyan Power Plant as compensation. Now, with the efforts of all parties, major textile mills will be able to resume their own power generation by next spring. The Qishuyan Power Plant will also receive a new generator and a wartime British generator, which will increase the electricity supply capacity. Therefore, the problem of insufficient power in Wuxi can be satisfactorily resolved in two or three months. In the past and present power allocation and dispatch, the Qishuyan Power Plant has indeed worked diligently and endured hardship.

The Executive Yuan is sending Guizhou refugees back to their hometowns, and their food and lodging along the way are provided by the agency (Executive Yuan photograph).

The First Vital Point on the Lifeline: A Snapshot of Changchun

— November 28th Airmail Report by Our Changchun Reporter, Fang Ren

Changchun is now like a patient suffering from anemia, a seriously ill person with paralysis on the left and right sides, and suffering from many ailments. It is a desert, and some say it is a pool of stagnant water.

Native-born, Locally Raised City Councilors Dare to Speak

First of all, I, as an audience member, must thank the establishment of the Provisional City Council of Changchun. It allows me to hear from those who are eloquent and articulate, reporting on their actual experiences of life over the years, or more seriously, reporting on their actual work over the years.

The Provisional City Council of Changchun was officially established on November 22nd. After its establishment, it continued to hold general meetings, which have not yet concluded. There are a total of thirty-one councilors. Eight of them come from the countryside because there are eight districts within the city limits of Changchun, and they are inhabited by farmers who make a living by farming. There are also representatives elected by labor unions, and their proposals and inquiries invariably emphasize the interests of workers as more sacred than the interests represented by any other representative. Elementary school teachers desperately exaggerate the importance of matters related to elementary school students. There are also two silver-bearded elders who insist that the five-hundred-person mixed-gender chorus organized by the city government during the Double Tenth Festival was "indecent" and the mingling of men and women was too unrefined. Several young fellows, when discussing the elimination of superstition during the passing of a proposal, shouted loudly, ordering the factories that make joss paper and the "slum dwellings" that make paper figures and horses to cease operations completely because they are the main culprits in promoting the existence of superstition! The reporter wants to particularly emphasize this point: indeed, there are quite a few councilors who have never seen the world. They are not only native-born in Northeast China, but also native-born in the rural areas of Northeast China. However, they dare to speak boldly. One thing is regrettable: among the thirty-one councilors, not one is female. Strangely, the female citizens in the audience have also been as rare as stars in the morning sky in recent days.

Two Slogans: Production is More Important Than Taxation; Developing Resources is More Important Than Cutting Costs

Relying solely on tax revenue is insufficient. Therefore, Director Xiao Renshu proposed two "slogans" as the standard for today's efforts to solve Changchun's financial problems: "Production is more important than taxation; developing resources is more important than cutting costs." What does it mean to create production and develop resources? According to Xiao's opinion: (1) Open up production enterprises, because although Changchun does not occupy an important position in the production industry in the Northeast, it is secondary. Most of these were contributed and established by the blood and sweat of the citizens, so a portion should be taken out for the public to enjoy. For example, if the Changchun Cigarette Factory were operated by the municipal government, the city's finances would have a great solution, but this factory was taken over by the Jilin Provincial Government. (2) Reorganizing real estate rents, a monthly income of twenty to thirty million yuan is not a problem, but those belonging to the central government were taken over by the central government; and those not belonging to the central government were taken over by the Real Estate Administration Bureau. (3) Establishing a municipal bank can make capital more flexible, unlike the national bank, which is subject to excessive restrictions. If the municipal bank converts current assets from the four major banks, this will naturally make the market prosperous, and the city's finances will naturally benefit from it. (4) Rectify tax collection so that the city's tax revenue can be fully accounted for, which will greatly benefit the city government. (5) Establish a trading market to prevent tax evasion on livestock, grain, etc. (6) Make good use of post-war relief materials. (7) Facilitate the flow of materials and strive to meet the requirements of smooth commodity circulation.

Police Reform: The Authorities Have Made Painstaking Efforts

In the Northeast, due to the influence of the enemy and puppet regime, "police" were always called together with "secret agents," and people in the Northeast couldn't help but feel disgust and hatred when "police" and "secret agents" were mentioned. Because in the hands of "police" and "secret agents," countless people were separated from their parents, children, and spouses under the names of "ideological criminals" and "economic criminals." They were thugs raised by the Japanese, creators of tragedies of life and death, demons who killed without blinking an eye, and complete bastards who only knew themselves and didn't know others.

After the central government took over the Northeast, the most difficult thing was the establishment of a new police administration. Because to make the people of Northeast China change their minds, it is necessary to completely sweep away all the bad habits of the past police as much as possible, and let these people-friendly police officers gain a new understanding from their new behaviors.

After the National Army entered Changchun at the end of May, it can be said that considerable effort was put into the rectification of the police administration. In addition to establishing a police training school starting on July 1, which has now trained three classes, with a total of 547 police officers after training, daily training is also implemented, with two hours of training each day, and training is also conducted during memorial weeks and various gatherings. However, after the police report, the councilors enthusiastically stood up to question, saying that on November 24, the police, while patrolling in the early morning, shot and killed an old man named Fu Shuming, who was holding a pickaxe and prying up the floor of an empty house near the Xiyang District. The police said: because they saw Fu coming with an object, "seeing the situation was not good, they opened fire," which is really suspected of committing a serious crime of recklessness. In addition, the police also accepted civil and criminal litigation cases in rural areas on the outskirts, beating and detaining people at will, and judging matters of "marriage and land" in a completely confused manner.

The Sins of the Big-Nosed Soldiers: Creating Suffering Between Young Couples

In the police report, there was one report that particularly caught everyone's attention. That report was a statistic, and that statistic was based on a survey of the things that the people of Changchun did not want to experience after the Soviet army entered Changchun. The statistics are: 28 rapes, 53 arson and killings, 2,842 lootings, and 16 destructions, totaling 2,939.

At the very moment when the Provisional City Council was meeting, such a bizarre thing happened in Changchun. It can be said to be one of the manifestations of the above statistics.

A young couple had a deep affection for each other. One dark night last winter, a big-nosed soldier broke into their house. Without explanation, he forcibly violated the woman and left. The young husband felt that this "disaster" was irresistible and still loved his wife. The wife originally wanted to die in anger, but seeing this, her love increased, and the two became even more "loving." Unfortunately, in October of this year, she suddenly gave birth to a son. The body and hair had many unusual characteristics. After a doctor's examination, it was proven to be a thoroughbred mixed-race child. The young husband couldn't help but wonder if fertilization was possible after forced sexual intercourse. The doctor replied that it was possible. But if this child is by their side, it will cause unpleasant feelings between the couple, and they want to put him to death. Friends advised: the little life itself is innocent, there is no need to kill. If this child really evokes sad memories, giving the child to others is also a solution.

Such things are endless. This can also explain one of the reasons why the compatriots in the Northeast are unhappy with certain people.

A Review of the Achievements of October

From "April 14" of this year back to December 22, 1945, this stage of the Changchun Municipal Government was engaged in taking over and promoting public administration under the occupation of the Soviet army. During this period, there are four things to mention:

(1) Organization of the Enemy and Puppet Industry Management Committee. This organization was composed of local gentry and various institutions and organizations convened by the municipal government. They jointly undertook the responsibility of managing enemy and puppet industries, compiling a clear list to avoid losses, and preparing to hand them over to the people sent by the central government who were responsible for the actual takeover.

(2) Organization of the Real Estate Adjustment Committee. This organization aimed to manage all enemy and puppet houses to prevent them from being occupied by others, and at the same time pay attention to allocating a portion of houses as residences for civilians.

(3) Preventing corruption. At the beginning of the takeover, there was a deep fear that unscrupulous officials would take the opportunity to commit fraud. As a result, one director and three takeover personnel were found guilty of dereliction of duty and were punished accordingly.

(4) Reorganization of the Baojia system. At the beginning of the restoration, it was impossible to talk about household registration and security. After the takeover, work began on this, with a total of more than 800,000 people. The situation at that time was quite successful.

From "May 23" to the present, the following points can be mentioned:

(1) Sending back Japanese expatriates and prisoners. Changchun did a considerable job in this matter. The work of repatriating Japanese expatriates and prisoners in the Northeast began on May 17, while Changchun began after the National Army entered. Changchun repatriated a total of more than 200,000 people.

(2) Implementation of Baomin and police patrols. This was to enable the people's strength to cooperate with the police during the winter defense period to carry out patrol duties and household registration checks. It is currently being actively promoted.

(3) Stabilizing prices, wages, and rents. All prices, wages, and rents are determined through price negotiations, with relevant groups jointly negotiating prices, which are then approved by the municipal government and implemented.

(4) Supporting cultural undertakings. In accordance with the orders of the central government, citizens enjoy extremely free speech and publication. Therefore, a considerable number of newspapers and magazines are published in Changchun.

(5) Appeasing young people. The Forward Command Post of the Commander-in-Chief jointly organized a youth summer training camp in the summer, which accommodated young people returning from the north of the Songhua River. It also solved employment problems for some of the trainees.

(6) Reorganizing the city's finances. In accordance with the instructions of the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters, simplifying administration and reducing personnel, and all non-urgent needs were temporarily postponed. At the same time, the city's finances were focused on increasing revenue and reducing expenditure.

(7) Improving public utilities and health undertakings. Improving tap water, paying particular attention to the cleanliness of drinking water. The city's trams and buses were completely destroyed in the war, but after active repairs, the number of vehicles running in the city has greatly increased. The prevention of epidemics is being handled with no regard for manpower and financial resources.

(8) Strengthening education. Changchun is not only seeking an increase in the number of students, but also improving the quality of teachers, and has held several teacher training sessions and strengthened normal schools.

(9) Improving the police administration. Changing police concepts, eliminating high-handed practices, improving service spirit, and cultivating patriotic consciousness. Especially in order to meet the requirements of Changchun's first priority of public security, all police facilities are mainly coordinated with military affairs.

(10) Cleaning up real estate and land administration construction. In the past, real estate files were unfortunately destroyed in the "April 14" fire, and much of the takeover work has not yet been completed. The property rights of enemy and puppet industries have not yet been determined, so a new Land Administration Bureau has been established, which will coordinate with the Finance Bureau to be responsible for cleaning up and adjusting land administration and real estate matters in the future.

The above are all the achievements reported. Of course, some are still in progress. However, the achievements of October can reveal some clues.

Looking to the Future: Changchun Has Its Own Future

Changchun is currently in suffering. But precisely because of this, people see its "desolate" current situation. Inevitably, there are many feelings. In reality, Changchun has its own "future." Looking ahead, Changchun really has a beautiful future.

Changchun is located in the center of nine provinces, is an important town in the Northeast, is the capital of the puppet Manchukuo, and is an important stronghold on the Sino-Soviet Railway connecting Europe and Asia. In a word, it is the first vital point on China's lifeline.

However, the serious fact at present is that the city's finances are insufficient. Such a grand city is plagued by poverty and confusion. If a fundamental solution to the financial resources is not thought of, the people of Changchun will be unable to maintain this city, unable to keep this city, built with the blood and sweat of the people of the Northeast, from changing its old appearance for a long time. Let alone reconstruction or anything else. Therefore, the councilors of the Provisional City Council suggest that Changchun be changed to a secondary capital, that Changchun be changed to a municipality directly under the Executive Yuan, and that the Commander-in-Chief's Headquarters be stationed in Changchun. Rather than looking at it from a positive perspective, saying that it is seeking to rebuild Changchun, it is more appropriate to look at it from a negative perspective, saying that it is seeking a solution to Changchun's financial resources. At the same time, the Provisional City Council also reported that although Shanghai and Tianjin are both municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan, they are also cities with a serious financial surplus. Therefore, Changchun's request to become a municipality directly under the Executive Yuan should be approved by the Executive Yuan.

Officers and Soldiers of the 184th Division: Captured and Escaped

During the battle to defend Dashiqiao, a portion of the officers and soldiers of the National Army's 184th Division were captured by the Communist Army. When Andong was recovered this time, the division, led by Regiment Commander Yang Chaolun, annihilated two battalions of rebel bandits, broke through the encirclement, and returned to Shenyang. The citizens held a general meeting to show their welcome. (Northeast Society Photograph)

The Key to Tainan: Penghu

— 4th Dispatch from He Minxian

Harbors Intertwined, Islands Stretching

Penghu Island's coastline meanders tortuously, with capes like intertwined dog teeth. The bay forms a peninsula, with an area of square miles. The 500-mile-long coastline faces Yuweng Island to the west, embracing a large bay. The water is deep enough to accommodate thousands of ships. Only the current Taiwan Strait is extremely dangerous. Ships sailing at sea must enter Penghu to take shelter in case of a storm to avoid capsizing. All major ports include Magong, Shili, Liangwen Port, Nanliao, Tudigongqian, Shashu, Zhenhai, Chihkan, Tongliang, Daguye, Zhugowan, Jima Creek, Nei'an, Qimen, Jiangjun'ao, Budai, and Shui'an, among others. The largest harbor is the east and west ao of Magong. The anchorage west of Xiangkou is 24 to 50 feet deep, with an area of 238,000 ping. Since ancient times, the Penghu Islands have been said to consist of 36 islands, 72 islets, 49, or 55. However, according to accurate surveys, there are only 64. It is said that although the total number of large and small islands and reefs reaches more than 60, only 44 of them can be called Yu Island. All of them can be divided into two groups: (A) the Penghu main island group (including Penghu Island, Baisha Island, Yuweng Island, and their affiliated islands). (B) the Bazhao Islands (including Bazhao Port, Jiangjunyu, Dongjiyu, Xijiyu, Dongyuping, Xiyuping, Dayu, Huayu, and their affiliated islands). The Penghu Islands are the collective name of the Penghu main island group and the Bazhao Islands. The main island (Dashan Island, i.e., Penghu Island) is in the center, Bazhao is in the south, Jibei Island is in the north, and Zha Po and Zha Mu Islands are in the east. In the west is Yuweng Island (Xiyu), with varying densities and sizes, forming a layered defense. As it is located at the key point of the Taiwan Strait, ships sailing nearby must use this island as a standard for their routes. However, the waves in the bay are surging, and the island's foot is densely covered with hidden reefs. It is not easy to moor without familiarity with the waterways. The names of each island are recorded as follows:

(A) Thirty-one islands in the northern part of the main island: (Baisha Island, Nanmiangua Island, Zhongdun Island, Jian Island, Jun Island, Baisha Island (same name two), Dakang Island, Yuanbei Island, Jibei Island, Wo Island, Daxue Island, Yanging Island, Jin Island, Maochang Island, Island, Xiao Island, Pingqi Island, Tudifeng Island, Jilong Island, Baisha Island (same name three), Cao Island (same name two), Xianjiao Island, Niumujian Island, Hai'an, Baisha Island, Tiezhen Island, Gupoyu Island, Maosi Island, Mudou Island, Quzhao Island, Beijiao.)

(B) Five islands in the eastern part of the main island: (Zha Po Island—Yang Island, Zha Mu Island—Yin Island, Xiangjin Island, Dingdiao Island, Jishan Island.)

(C) Twenty islands in the southern part of the main island: (Bazhao Island, Jinguazai, Jiangjun'ao, Yuhou, Dizi, Toujin, Liyue, Ma'anshan Island, Gousha Island, Chuanfan Island, Da Island, Xiyuping, Dongyuping, Zhongzai Island, Dongji Island, Hua Island, Xiaomao Island, Damao Island, Chutou Island, Cao Island (same name two).

(D) Five islands in the western part of the main island: (Cetian Island—Xiao Yan Island, Tongpan Island, Xiaomen Island, Hujing Island, Yuwei Island—Xiyu.)

Among the above islands, there are the most in the northern part, with 31, and the least in the eastern and western parts, with 5 each. As for the comparison of area, the main island has an area of more than square miles, and the area of the 63 affiliated islands combined also reaches more than square miles, similar to the main island, which is extremely coincidental. As for the origin of the island names, most of them are named after their shapes. The easternmost island is Zha Mu Island, the westernmost is Hua Island, the southernmost is Da Island, and the northernmost is Mudou Island.
