Published by the publishing industry every Thursday.

The Ethics of Writing

— Chuantong Xian

Recently, this magazine received a contribution discussing a "Chemical Calculation Method" published in 1939 by Kaiming, which has recently been copied and published using a clever method of disguise. The analysis and comparison between the two are quite detailed, but unfortunately, it could not be published due to space limitations. However, this made me think about the ethics of writers. Writing is a very arduous task. If someone makes a living by writing, that is already a dead end. If someone steals and exploits, that is simply heartless.

This also reminds me of a lawsuit ten years ago between two bookstores because the English textbooks published by the two were similar. Some people say that Chinese people have a problem, which is that they do not know how to create through their own efforts. When they see that others have achieved slight success or a slight profit in a certain aspect, they rise up to imitate and counterfeit. For example, no one in Shanghai knows which Lu Song Company is real. What is strange is that this phenomenon also occurs in the publishing industry, which has a higher level of Chinese culture. Why can't we strive for improvement and strive for excellence? We must find ways to extinguish this mentality of speculation and opportunism.

The Chinese publishing industry is extremely lacking in both material and spiritual aspects. This is undeniable. Therefore, on the one hand, we hope that people with capital will engage in the publishing industry, and the government will try to support them (such as providing loans and exempting sales tax on publications). On the other hand, writers should enrich their own content, work hard in research, and maintain a noble personality. At the very least, we must maintain the minimum level of writing ethics.

An Introduction to "A True History of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom"

— Luo Hongtao

By Guo Tingyi

Published by the Commercial Press

Over 1400 pages

Price: 18,000 yuan

The Heavenly Capital of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom fell to the Qing army on July 19, 1864 (corresponding to the 16th day of the sixth month of the third year of the Tongzhi reign). More than eighty years have passed since its demise, yet there is still no complete record of this great revolutionary movement, truly a great disgrace for historians. Now, the publication of Mr. Guo's book is just enough to make up for this major deficiency, truly a great blessing for the academic world. It is noted that people's views on the historical facts of the Taiping can be divided into four periods. From its demise onwards, the Qing court from top to bottom, as well as British and French imperialists, jointly engaged in malicious counter-propaganda, denigrating the Taiping army as even worse than bandits and brigands. At the same time, the populace fabricated various imagined cruel events, which marks the first period. Around the time of the founding of the Republic of China, the revolutionary atmosphere was already stirring, and the general public recognized the Taiping army as revolutionary martyrs. Consequently, various historical materials were fabricated (such as Mr. Liu Yazi's statement on August 20, the 23rd year of the Republic of China, that the original manuscript of Shi Dakai's poetry collection was compiled by his exiled friend Gao Tianmei. Much of it was fabricated, mostly by Tianmei, as propaganda for the revolution at the time, borrowing literature as a tool). Moreover, based on imagination, events such as Hong Xiuquan being a disciple of Zhu Jiu, Hong Daquan being named the Prince of Heavenly Virtue, and Qian Jiang submitting a memorial, appeared, creating seemingly true but false historical events, which marks the second period. In the ninth year of the Republic of China, Liu Niu Chenruo copied and printed sixteen interesting documents of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom from the British Museum. From then on, more and more people began to unearth Taiping historical materials from overseas. Mr. Cheng Yansheng from the library of the School of Oriental Languages in Paris; Mr. Xiao Yishan from the Oriental Department of the British Museum in London; Mr. Wang Chongmin from the library of Cambridge University in England; and Mr. Yu Dawei from the Prussian State Library in Berlin, all had significant harvests. (According to scholars, among the four mentioned above, Mr. Xiao's acquisitions were the most numerous, while Mr. Yu's were the most refined. Mr. Yu's portion, proofread by Mr. Zhang Jusheng, was compiled into my humble edition of "Taiping Heavenly Kingdom Poetry and Prose Collection," but it is now out of print.) Furthermore, the Palace Museum in China also unearthed original historical materials, long hidden for a century, now reappearing to aid research, which is no small contribution. This marks the third period. However, although researching the historical facts of the Taiping became a fad among historians, what they obtained were only fragments. No one was able to conduct comprehensive research. That is, until Mr. Guo's book. In the preface, Mr. Luo Jialun states that Mr. Guo spent over a decade silently working on this issue before achieving this great harvest. Mr. Guo himself is modest, considering this book to be a historical record of tools, only seeking to prepare the way for others, hoping that historians with talent and scholarship can use it to create a complete record. This marks the fourth period. Objectively speaking, Mr. Guo's work is successful in the present situation.

This book's record of events begins in the first year of the Jiaqing reign and ends in the seventh year of the Tongzhi reign. In addition to specifically recording the history of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom and the Nian Rebellion, it also describes the background of this great turmoil as much as possible, such as the turmoil during the Jiaqing and Daoguang reigns, peasant uprisings in various places, and the activities of the Tiandihui (Heaven and Earth Society) and the Sanhehui (Triads), all within the scope of the record. The recorded facts consider all sides, but due to limitations of materials, military battles account for the majority. The facts are recorded in chronological order. The months and days recorded include both the Chinese and Western calendars, and the new calendar implemented by the Taiping army is also noted where it can be verified. The facts of the months and days are strived to be accurate. For those involving doubts, various sources are consulted for textual research, truly worthy of being called an excellent work. At the same time, the author believes that local chronicles contain some important materials that cannot be found elsewhere, so they are used as much as possible. This is a new path opened for those studying Taiping history. Although he was able to borrow reference books from Tsinghua, Central, Yenching, and Jinling Universities, as well as the libraries of the Central Political, Beiping, and Nanjing National Studies institutions, and had good support, his spirit of research is also admirable.

The main text of this book is worth praising, and the eight appendices are also worth introducing.

The first appendix is a comparison table of the Taiping calendar and the lunar calendar, as well as a brief table of days of the week. Several people had done this work before Mr. Guo. However, the Heavenly Calendar's sexagenary cycle does not match the lunar calendar's sexagenary cycle, differing by one day. Also, the Taiping day of the week does not match the Western day of the week, also being one day earlier. Due to these two differences, the previous work was completely abandoned. Mr. Guo's table, however, is worth quoting and guaranteed to be error-free.

The second appendix is a table of figures from the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom, which is simply a small-scale biography of Taiping historical figures. It begins with explanations of titles and ranks, with detailed textual research. Each table is divided into items such as title, name, place of origin, experience, birth and death, and notes. The recorded events are rich, easy to check, and suitable for application.

The third appendix is a table of generals in major battles. Each battle records its main generals, subordinates, location, and opposing generals. There are a total of eighteen tables on the Taiping army side and seven tables on the Qing army side. These twenty-five tables cannot be written without having the entire historical facts organized in one's mind. What a rare effort.

The fourth appendix consists of fourteen maps of the wars between the Hong (Taiping) and Qing armies. "Left map, right history" was valued in ancient times. With these maps, reading history becomes even more interesting. Mr. Luo Jialun also states in his preface that the method of attaching maps comes from modern concepts. It would not be possible without the progress of modern technology.

The fifth appendix is a table of Qing ministers and officials. The sixth appendix is a table of commanders who suppressed the Nian Rebellion. Both tables record items such as office, name, term of office, original position, location of residence, and notes, which helps in checking. The seventh appendix is a brief record of generals from both the Hong and Qing sides, which is extensively collected and recorded.

The eighth appendix is a bibliography. The books listed are limited to those that Mr. Guo has referred to and used as a basis for compilation. The books are divided into two parts: one is Chinese, totaling 197 types, plus 380 types of local chronicles, and 8 types of periodicals; the other is Western, totaling 43 types. After each entry, a brief explanation and commentary are added to clarify its nature. There are over six hundred books cited, but what the author can say is that Mr. Guo's table is not to flaunt his collection, but Mr. Guo has actually cited them one by one. This is what makes it so valuable.

Finally, it must be stated that Mr. Guo's book is indispensable for those studying Taiping history. Mr. Xiao Yishan is a leading authority on Qing history and has also made many contributions to Taiping historiography, possessing the largest collection of Taiping historical books. Mr. Guo's book should have been read by him long ago. However, in recent correspondence, it is known that he still regrets not having seen this book. Even an expert is like this, let alone others. Therefore, not avoiding the risk of being meddlesome, I wrote this article to introduce it.

A Masterpiece of Human Geography: The Geographical Basis of China

— Junzhi

By George Babcock Cressey, Translated by Xue Yiyuan

Published by Kaiming Bookstore, September of the 35th year of the Republic of China

The relationship between geography and human life is the closest. To understand the various human relationships in China, it can be said that we need to rely on the study of geography, because only through it can we understand the factors of agriculture, resources, climate, region, and human life.

Professor George Babcock Cressey, the author of this book, resided in China for a long time, completing this work after more than ten years of research and travel; at the same time, this work is also the result of his more than ten years of hard work. The author serves in China as a visiting professor under the Cultural Affairs Bureau of the United States Department of State and as a representative in China for the American Council of Learned Societies and the National Academy of Sciences; due to these many conveniences, the research work he conducts is even better than that of us Chinese. Our Chinese geographers have absolutely no opportunity to conduct research for such a long time and spend so much money. Therefore, although the author is an American, this book is still a relatively accomplished new geography work in Chinese geography.

Today, this book is worth reading whether or not one is a geographer, just as the author said in the original preface: "China is now in the midst of unprecedented social, economic, and political adjustments. A great power that has always been isolated and conservative is now quickly reforming its life and becoming a member of the world's nations. Geography cannot claim to be able to solve some of the problems arising from evolution, but it can explain some of the background to this evolution."

The Social Geographical Foundation

This volume, "The Geographical Basis of China," is the general theory part of George Babcock Cressey's geographical works on China, divided into six parts: geographical overview, topography, climate, farmers, natural resources, and world communication, for separate explanations.

Now, let's look at its contents: In the first chapter, "Geographical Landscape," it points out that the most important factor in China's landscape is not soil, plants, or climate, but the people. This point, we can trust, in China's ancient land, it is difficult to find a small place that has not been rendered by human activities. At the same time, the author also points out China's natural isolation. In the past history, China has been surrounded by obstructive barriers, and has not been in contact with other parts of the world, and the exchange of knowledge is also very little. These are the tropical jungles, tall mountains, vast deserts, and distant oceans that jointly maintain China's unity and isolation.

Thomas said in "The Foundations of Social Environment": "It is now generally recognized that the most important factor in cultural progress is the contact of multiple cultures, and stagnation occurs if isolated. A certain environment is sufficient to touch another environment and provide a path, mutually communicating with another area, which will encourage the receptivity of people's minds and the progress of culture; conversely, an isolated environment will inevitably cause mental stagnation and repetition."

From this, we can understand the reasons for the backwardness of Chinese science.

This chapter also describes contrasting places, outlining a comparison table between the South and the North, population pressure; and explaining new and old transportation, listing examples of cars and highways in various places.

The author's conclusion in this chapter, the paragraph "China in Understanding," is inaccurate in several places because the writing era is different. But as a reference, it is extremely valuable.

The Relationship Between Climate and Farmland

The second chapter, "Topography," explains the geological foundation; China certainly does not have the glacial features of Europe and North America, so the author lists our characteristics. These cannot be introduced one by one here.

In addition, regarding mountains, rivers, alluvial plains, coastal areas, and changes in China's territory, the author uses very sufficient materials to explain; and lists the population and area surveys of various provinces in China for reference.

Climate - the factor that determines human activity, is discussed in the third chapter of this book. It describes the physical nature of China's climate, which is the monsoon operation that is transformed sequentially by topography and ocean relations, occasional tropical cyclones, and a series of continental storms, to produce a climate zone. Climate and human life are also fully elaborated, as well as wind direction illustrations and tables of average temperature and average rainfall.

Chapter Four is about "Farmers for Four Thousand Years." Of course, China has always been known as an agricultural country, and agricultural issues are the most important. In this chapter, the author first explains the morning landscape, then touches on the foundation of agriculture, and the broad expanse of Chinese arable land. He lists and explains the arable land of past dynasties and the arable land of various provinces, and further reports the detailed table of arable land and crop area of each province. There is also a table explaining crop yields.

China's agricultural problems still exist today. The author points out the general importance of China's agricultural problems in the past. The scientification of Chinese fish farming requires social transformation. After the basic knot of the current situation is untied, we can embark on this path.

The issue of natural resources is discussed in Chapter Five. It first discusses the historical background; the source of coal and the world's coal reserves, extending to the most important power - coal mining. Then, the estimated coal reserves and the coal production of various mines are listed and explained separately.

Regarding other power sources, such as oil, iron, and other metallic and non-metallic substances, explanations are also accompanied by tables; finally, the production of Chinese minerals and the prospects of Chinese industry are discussed.

Looking Forward to China's Trade

The last chapter is "China's Interaction with the World." The author describes its historical background. China's earliest westward expeditions and trade began during the reign of Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty. By the nineteenth century, export trade gradually increased, and it is listed to explain the goods directly exported to foreign countries and the comparison of foreign trade commodities.

Weaving trade is certainly far greater than export trade. This is after the Opium War, international capitalism opened up China's independent and autonomous gate, creating the sub-colonial status mentioned by Sun Yat-sen. The author of this book also points out: "For many years, tangible imports have greatly exceeded the value of exports. This so-called unfavorable trade balance has become increasingly harmful in recent years."

Finally, it explains China's trading ports and the foreign trade of various ports. At this point, the book comes to an end.

After reading this book, one has a basic understanding of China's geography. Therefore, this book can be used as a basic understanding for young people in study.

The Museum of Modern Art in New York, in addition to displaying representative works of famous individuals, also organizes collective exhibitions based on various schools. The image shows a part of the museum's sculpture exhibition hall.

Rereading "Fathers and Sons"

— Xin Jun

By Ivan Turgenev, Translated by Ba Jin

Published by Cultural Life Press, September of the 35th year of the Republic of China, 365 pages

In the field of literature and art, French romantic literature, with its gorgeous writing style, has attracted a wide range of readers. From this, we think of Turgenev, a famous writer. His novels and prose poems have intoxicated countless young people. Turgenev himself was Russian and of aristocratic descent. However, he studied in France, so his works could not escape the color of French romanticism.

Turgenev's works mostly take the resistance of young people against the old forces in the era of the Russian Tsarist regime as the theme. However, he only describes it from the side, using his skillful writing and the soul of "nihilism" to depict those immortal figures in literature and art.

The novel "Fathers and Sons" depicts the conflict between new and old ideas in the era of the liberation of Russian serfs, using his beautiful style and developing it through the prism of his view of life.

The content of this novel is roughly about:

A progressive landlord, a descendant of the Russian aristocracy—Nikolai, and his son—Arkady, who is returning home from the University of St. Petersburg, this pair of father and son are the central figures. The author develops a magnificent masterpiece from the personalities of the two of them.

Arkady is a hollow believer in nihilism, and the one who gave him this belief is his classmate Bazarov; this time he came home with Bazarov as a companion. Therefore, he criticizes all of his old father Nikolai's actions with his nihilistic eyes, which sometimes makes his old father feel very uncomfortable.

Nikolai has an older brother, Pavel, who is a complete maintainer of aristocratic dignity, a stubborn old man, so Bazarov often argues with him.

After many days, two like-minded nihilists met a beautiful lady, Anna, at a welcome party; consequently, they unknowingly fell into the city of love, and all their actions and deeds in front of Anna seemed to be somewhat different from the past.

After the two nihilists entered Anna's manor together, Bazarov gained victory. Arkady, however, was also very enthusiastic about Anna's sister, Katya.

Soon, the two of them felt that it was not worth spending time only in the horn of love. So they broke away from the entanglement of love and went to live in Bazarov's home at the same time. Bazarov's father was an enlightened small serf. After they arrived there, the shackles of love did not break away from them; Arkady ran to Anna's manor on the pretext, while Bazarov thought of Nikolai's beloved concubine, Feni, and went to Nikolai's home, and got the opportunity to kiss Feni twice.

This secret was known by Nikolai's stubborn brother Pavel, who was furious and agreed to a duel with Bazarov. In the end of the duel, the stubborn old man was injured. Because of this lesson, the old man changed his previous stubbornness and compromised with the new trend.

Bazarov could no longer live in Nikolai's home; after he left, he ran to Anna's place to tell Arkady about this, and also met Anna, and finally returned to his father's manor.

Here, Nikolai, due to the persuasion of his changed brother, broke the concept of class and officially held a wedding with Feni. Arkady also succeeded in love with Anna's sister, and married on the same day as his father.

Fathers and sons combined two pairs of newlyweds on the same auspicious day; afterwards, the father and son jointly operated agriculture and did very well; the families were also very harmonious. In that beautiful and happy environment, they lived a sweet life.

What about Bazarov? After he returned home, he worked as a doctor for the farmers, but one time he was careless in dissecting and contracted a terrible disease, ending his life.

Bazarov's parents often mourned and wept before their son's spirit.

This masterpiece ends here on its last page.

After reading this work, it is very clear that it uses the ups and downs of love as a clue, fully expressing the atmosphere of romanticism and its unreality. In the entanglement of love, various thoughts are silent.

Bazarov, originally a forward-thinking person, encounters obstacles and suffers everywhere here. As a result, he destroyed himself.

Arkady, although a worshiper of Bazarov, was not as unruly; he was loved by his father and uncle, and as a result also became a follower of his career.

What about Nikolai? His progressive thinking cooperated with his son and entered a pink and happy family; his brother also reformed a stubborn aristocratic self-esteem and achieved compromise.

This work cannot be denied to have its skillful beauty in terms of literary depiction. The conclusion is also called perfect. Only in terms of consciousness, as mentioned earlier, it cannot match the facts and is full of philistine ways.

It writes a forward-thinking young man with a satirical pen as destroying himself, while on the aristocratic side, the author is sympathetic. Pavel's compromise and the sweet life of Nikolai and his son are the opposite of Bazarov.

The writing style of this work is worth learning, because this work is a very good masterpiece as a common work of art. The translator Ba Jin translated it based on the English version, and the translation is fairly smooth, but it may not be completely consistent with the original text. In short, this is a beautifully depicted work of art!

Concerning the Soviets

— Jiuzhang

A. WHITE: A REPORT ON THE RUSSIANS

The author of this book, Mr. White, visited the Soviet Union in the summer of 1944 when the relationship between the United States and the Soviet Union was extremely harmonious. He was "specially permitted" to "see what he wanted to see and write what he wanted to write after returning home." He visited the Maral industrial area in the Soviet hinterland, a place that no foreigner had been to since the beginning of the Five-Year Plan in 1926. He entered the newly recovered rural areas of Ukraine, talking to farmers, hoping to hear their true inner thoughts. Of course, there were also one or two times when the iron fist of ideological control prevented Mr. White from visiting freely. They visited a factory in Siberia, where he had a very pleasant conversation with a German-speaking female worker. However, as soon as White turned around, a secret police officer (NKVD, formerly GPU) questioned her. From then on, she only responded with reluctant agreement or silence. "In the Soviet Union, where can anyone freely talk to foreigners?" But, on the whole, Mr. White's group's visit was quite free. Especially during his debate with a female translator in Moscow, he frankly stated where he thought the Soviet Union was inferior to the United States; the frankness was probably surprising to the reader.

What I personally am particularly interested in is what is the life of the average Soviet person actually like? The author of this book happens to have this point of view: he does not vaguely discuss Soviet policies, but often wants to know the daily expenses of a worker. The standard of living of ordinary people is an achievement of governance and cannot be considered a military secret. Treating such information as a military secret, thereby arousing suspicion, is always an unwise move.

In the third chapter, the author describes his visit to three Moscow factories: an aircraft factory, an automobile factory, and a biscuit factory. In the first factory, he inquired about working hours and wages. The working hours of ordinary workers are sixty-six hours per week, and the income is one thousand rubles. Eating a meal in the factory cafeteria costs five rubles a day, which is very cheap. But what can you buy with the remaining eight hundred or more rubles per month? In the "store," ham costs more than one thousand rubles per pound, and chicken costs around five hundred rubles per pound. Clothing is even more expensive. Therefore, this worker can fill his stomach by eating in the factory cafeteria and pass a few evenings by going to the designated theater, but "once he leaves the factory, his food and clothing immediately become a problem." He cannot save money like an American. Mr. White said, "The factory is theoretically owned by the workers, but in reality, the workers belong to the factory."

In the second factory, Mr. White asked the "manager" what happens if workers are lazy at work. "First, a warning is posted on the wall newspaper, and then a speech is given at the trade union." Mr. White immediately understood! The trade union has become an organization to restrain workers. Another time (Chapter 8), White asked a trade union leader, if a worker is dissatisfied with his current job, can he go somewhere else? The answer was, "He must apply to the factory." "If he leaves without permission, can he find work elsewhere?" The answer was, "No, he will have a very hard time finding work anywhere in the Soviet Union." Mr. White also asked, "Isn't this equivalent to a blacklist?" The answer was, "It can't be considered a blacklist." The "freedom" in the American mind cannot be found in the Soviet dictionary. As for the author's comparison of the lives of Soviet workers to the lives of American prisoners in Chapter 4, perhaps it is a bit too indignant. By analogy, "the treatment of workers throughout the Soviet Union is almost the same, because all factories belong to the government, and the treatment is all stipulated by the government." Some Chinese readers may agree with this approach, but Americans generally cannot accept it.

"In the Soviet Union, the lives of employed workers are not as good as the lives of workers receiving unemployment benefits during the economic panic in the United States." It is difficult to say how reliable this statement is. But the words of the Soviet female translator in the book can only be regarded as "self-deprecating." She said, "I am very miserable myself, but I know that everyone else is miserable, and I am comforted." Everyone with common sense knows that the slogan of socialism is to realize "everyone's paradise," not everyone being equally poor. There will always be a gap between the slogan and the reality. An ideal will always change somewhat when it is put into practice. This was the case before and after the French Revolution, and it is also true of the Russian Revolution.

The author has not studied the economic systems of the United States and the Soviet Union. He can only briefly talk about the shortcomings of the Soviet Union as perceived by Mr. White. (1) It is very difficult for the Soviet government to plan and guide the activities and development of factories across the country from one center (the Kremlin). The "managers" or responsible persons of each factory tend to be perfunctory and lack initiative, and some technical and management talents are sometimes purged due to political lines. (2) The elimination of the profit motive reduces competition, and people generally do not want to improve production methods. According to Mr. White, the American system has a greater incentive for new inventions than the Soviet system. The Stakhanovite movement was actually secretly restoring competition, but the encouragement of "medals" is not as good as actual benefits. "Generally speaking, capitalism invents, and socialism imitates." This is White's view.

However, what is read in the book, that is, what the author saw, is that the Soviet Union also has many advantages. For example, the standard of living of Soviet people is lower than that of Americans, but there are no beggars. During wartime, resources are always first used by frontline soldiers. As well as the Soviet government's handling of issues among ethnic minorities, etc. The author has never denied this.

Books such as "Impressions" or "Memoirs" have become an important category in British and American books. The writing is fluent, like a novel; the observations are unique, enough for experts to pick from. This book is also like this. But our post-war publishing industry rarely sees this type of book for the time being.

Publishing News

"War and Peace" by Tolstoy, jointly translated by Guo Moruo and Gao Di, and "Jean-Christophe" by Romain Rolland, translated by Fu Lei, are both immortal masterpieces in the world literary scene. These two books are currently being typeset by Camel Bookstore, and special-price pre-orders are being accepted from today until the 31st.

Spring and Autumn

Introducing [Meng Jiangnv]

— Wang Bosheng

As early as twenty-one years ago, while engaged in research and improvement work on inherent and modern theater arts in Beiping, I happened to see the premiere performance of Mr. Afu Xialomufu's opera at the Zhenguang Cinema. Twelve years ago, at the Shandong Provincial Theater, I had been involved in the pilot performance of the opera "Yue Fei." Not long ago, at the National Opera School, along with Zheng Zhisheng, Lin Gangbai, Chen Tianhe, Zhu Chongzhi, and many friends in the music and dance circles, I also engaged in the experimental performance of the operas "Jing Ke," "Xuan Zheng Gong," and "Song of China." Today, the "Meng Jiangnv" by Afu Xialomufu and Chen Zhong and others has also been staged in Beijing, Shanghai, and other places. Some of the performers this time are former colleagues and classmates. They all told me that this time the approach is the same as our previous experiments, both in theory and in the application of techniques. Therefore, I have watched it twice and will give a solemn introduction and explanation of its constituent principles and its influence on political philosophy and art philosophy.

I.

Why should we introduce this type of art? From the perspective of political philosophy, since the Three Dynasties, China has been influenced by feudal ideas, and the realm of national thought has gradually had invisible constraints. As a result, society has become increasingly rational, and a certain attitude and belief have been created in the minds of the vast society and the people. Therefore, the culture itself has entered a stage of stagnation for two thousand years. This invisibly morbid society, in the past hundred years, has felt the pressure from the international community in various economic aspects. As a result of rationalization, it has become increasingly impoverished, thus naturally forming selfishness, infighting, and fragmentation, causing society to fall into a state of collapse, fragmentation, and disunity. This is one of the reasons why Sun Yat-sen engaged in revolutionary work. After the revolution, followed by a difficult war of resistance, it has finally been completed. In terms of political and other improvements before and after the war, all staff members who were aware of the overall situation have done their best under the daily supervision of the leader. However, they still cannot reverse the declining trends of society. There are other reasons for this.

As far as I can see, the way to revitalization in the future is science and art. The importance of science is well known, but the importance of art, which outweighs science, is not easily understood by the general public. For example, take the industrial products of natural science. The more truthful the natural laws found in the universe are, the greater the power and the more contributions to mankind. However, no matter whether it is an atomic bomb or an airplane, its properties and power are ultimately limited. After all, it is mankind that controls and shakes the universe. The reason is that mankind has a subtle soul. Therefore, in ancient times, when governing a country, people's spiritual life and the human body, the so-called dwelling place of the soul, were nourished in all aspects of clothing, food, housing, and transportation. (Rites) were used as the basis for their political measures. Therefore, their political philosophy is: rites regulate people's hearts, music harmonizes people's voices, politics is implemented, and punishment is used to prevent. Rites, music, punishment, and politics reach all directions without contradiction, then the kingly way is fully prepared. From this, we know that punishment and politics are inevitable measures, and rites and music are essential components of life. (Rites are nourishment and should be viewed as the regulation of time and space art. As for human affairs, it is merely the measure between people. Please refer to Sima Qian's "Treatise on Rites and Music" in the "Records of the Grand Historian".)

Natural science has reached such a complex stage, so the art of cultivating people's minds must also make parallel progress with the functions of natural science to produce balanced effects. For example, ancient sedan chairs, no matter how good they are, no one rides in them anymore, because their functions are too far from those of airplanes and trains. Therefore, some of the functions of ancient rites and music should be replaced by musical dramas, because music must enter the drama to stimulate people's hearts and respond to people's rhythms. We really cannot think that it is just a kind of decoration for life because there is a word "drama." Because opera is a powerful organism, the use of lines and colors is the creation of visual science in the human spirit, and rhythm and melody are the creation of auditory science in the human soul. All progressive art is the science of cultivating the soul. Only with good cultivation of the soul can heat occur between people, can people's minds become broad, can they have resilience and compassion, can society become active and have new vitality. Therefore, any country with scientific development in Europe and America must also be a country with developed art, because society is peaceful and science has a foundation. If the spirit does not enter the right track, society cannot hope for peace and order. There are mutual effects. This is one of the reasons why this art career should be valued.

II.

From the perspective of the art philosophy of the times, Chinese society has fallen into a stage of rational poverty. If art is engaged in provocation or giving divergent hints, the people who are directly harmed are the masses. In response to the historical fact that the past feudal society has given us society too much manifestation of intelligence, it seems that we cannot but seek something in the creation of emotional art. Because society cannot be improved by simply destroying it, nor can it be effective by simply whipping it.

Next, I want to say a few words from the point of view of creation, because this is necessary for the analysis of the play "Meng Jiangnv." Every great art is a beautiful realm in itself, with an inviolable style. Only with this style can it influence people. A beautiful realm must have its constituent elements. In terms of music, because there is rhythm, it can transcend reality. Because it transcends reality, people can forget its ugliness. A beautiful realm and a great style, in terms of opera, its success often does not belong to the success of one kind of expression medium, because it must be a balanced development of various expression media to produce an organic organization of spiritual and physical harmony. But there are exceptions sometimes. If a certain expression medium has its unique beauty, it can also gradually induce other expression media to coordinate with it, and gradually form a complete organization. For example, the human soul is innate, and the coordination of its clothing and actions is governed by the soul. Although a kind of decoration sometimes makes it difficult for people to distinguish between truth and falsehood, it is indeed not an easy task for an opera artist to grasp the method of opening up and completing affairs. The merit and blame of Meng Jiangnv's music and dance lie in the fact that there is a considerable foundation for the application of this kind of coordination.

What is the independent style of Chinese music? This is the first question to be studied. China is a society of ethics and morality, so in music, emotions are not created by music, but ethics is created by medicine. In terms of the composition of ethics and morality, all arts in its society have their own independent forms based on this. There is a beginning, a middle, and an end. Most of them are expressions of transcendence of reality, peace, and personality. Its value is not so much focused on emotion as it is on personality. For example, bells are used to establish martial arts, bamboo is used to establish meetings, drums are used to establish movement, and chimes are used to establish discrimination. The reason why we cherish our percussion instruments lies only in this. In terms of the times, the weakness of Chinese music has been completely swallowed up by the torrent of its times. Mr. Afu Xialomufu picked up things that had been forgotten for a long time and gave them rich emotions and the power of the times, making a unique Chinese language (music is the language of the world) become the language of the world. This is indeed something worth cherishing. The chapters of Meng Jiangnv's music could be strengthened to create its main melody so that its character would be more powerful or even more distinctive.

Regarding actions, I believe that in the eyes of artists, there is no distinction between new, old, superior, or inferior for all of his expressive mediums, because most new things come from changes in the old. What artists need to consider carefully is the balance of power, the harmony of colors, the distance of scales, and the speed of rhythms. In terms of action, rhythm and lines are the expressive mediums of its power. This rhythm can achieve a consistent harmony with music, installations, drama texts, and other related aspects, and it must be successful. Chinese inherent drama and Indian drama have many similarities. The main thing is action. Gan Geoli exchanged opinions with Zhongnong two years ago. He deeply admired the use of action to represent words in Chinese drama. I believe that in drama, it is necessary to further develop what we already have, because in art, it is still a new inspiration. In the performance of "Yue Fei" in the past, I made expressions of coordination and non-coordination in action, and made a balanced development with the harmony of music. Sometimes its function exceeded that of music, because action is, after all, much more distinct than music. Chen Zhong, who actually performed the directing task of "Meng Jiangnv," has spent a lot of effort, which can be seen. I still hope that they will work harder so that the guest and host are distinct, there is a climax, the changes in the patterns can be increased again, and the use of movement and stillness can be more appropriate to strengthen the creation of its character. Then, a new harmonious introduction to inherent art can be established in the modern theater world.

In terms of installations, its style is generally quite harmonious, but the center of gravity of each painting should still be strengthened so that all sublimating effects transcend reality and have a basis.

In terms of costumes, it is also quite gorgeous, and no major problems can be seen. If we can not stick to historical facts and add more expression of character or make it more vivid in the lines and colors based on historical facts.

In terms of drama texts, the dialogue of the whole play should be changed to poetry. Its punctuation does not need to follow the inherent yin, yang, ping, qu, and ru tones (as in the old dramas), but should be created in terms of light and heavy speaking based on emotion. As for the structure of the whole play, the climax of each act and the climax of the whole play should be strengthened to make it a three-dimensional form to accommodate all the techniques.

I think all problems are easy to change now that she has established a commendable scale because these are all minor problems.

From a political point of view and from the point of view of art philosophy, it must be said that the performance of "Meng Jiangnv" is a work that is most worthy of cherishing. Because under the same principles, our ancient great epics and all cultural and artistic traces can be used as an opportunity to further express ourselves to people at home and abroad. Although this kind of creation is not something we cannot grasp ourselves, the revision of musical art is, after all, a task for a genius and requires long-term efforts. Afu Xialomufu has been in China for thirty years. He is welcome to work for the cause of art. Handel was a German who lived in England and became famous. His Messiah oratorio, because of the reverence of the King of England, became a beautiful story in the world. Chopin was a Pole who also lived in France and became famous because art is the common property of mankind. As for the plot of the drama, it can be seen that Qin Shihuang was selfish and did not care about the hunger of the people. He only wanted to achieve the desire of one family for a long-lasting foundation. He made this brutal and inhumane act that violated the public by destroying everything of the people and sacrificing it for one person and one surname to build the Great Wall, then Wan Xiliang and Meng Jiangnv were just representatives of the whole people. The sufferers were all families like this. If we face reality, then after this war, when the people of the world are suffering, all countries are suffering from using all their strength to expand their armaments again, then this play cannot but be said to be a most meaningful contribution to saving peace and saving the world, because the most precious thing about it is that it influences people with the style of art.

It is easier to see mistakes than truth, because mistakes are on the outside. So it is easy to see, but truth is at the bottom. Most people are unwilling to look for it.

Nude Woman

— Dai Lakewa

Dai Lakewa (E. Deracroin 1798-1864) was a traitor among the students of the early French classical writer David. Not only did he not inherit from his teacher, but he also established the Romantic school, causing a great revolution in the art world and enlightening later generations to establish painting theories. His style is novel, the colors are complex, and the subjects are mostly legends, myths, and history. "Dante's Boat Crossing" is one of his representative works. This nude woman was modeled after a maid in the court at that time. The brushstrokes are simple and solid (Lion).

Fiddler

— Li Jinming

Yan Dong Hutong is in the West City of Beiping. Even the most detailed map does not list its name. In this secluded neighborhood, besides a few jujube trees at the corner of the wall, in the summer season, you only hear the calls of those selling fruits—the rhythmic clanging of copper coins. On winter nights, Muslims chanted with a long voice: "Aluo sheep moon..."

At the western end of the alley is the city wall. The mule cart road is always so gray, deep and thick; crows gather in flocks on the power lines, among the weeds on the city wall. Only the fish-white sky is a suitable sight in the line of sight.

Especially in autumn, I developed a love of change for this environment. I often carried a lacquered cane that was convenient for use as a self-defense weapon and strolled to the vicinity of the city wall. It was strange that I didn't know why I was interested in visiting such a gray scene.

One day after Mid-Autumn Festival, I followed the old road and walked to the city wall, planning to go a little further north to find the stone steps that could be used to climb the city for sightseeing. I met a short, fat man in a blue cloth gown. His head, like a steamed bun, was shaved very clean. His right hand was holding a few pieces of tofu held by a lotus leaf, and his left hand was carrying a bottle of sesame oil. He smiled at me and said:

"Sixth Master, you are really funny. Why are you wandering around here?"

I looked at him for a while.

"Have you forgotten me?" he said, putting on an imposing look and choking on phlegm. "Haven't you heard what Qu Ziqiu of Hua District plays? I live diagonally across from your master's house."

Oh, that's right, his surname is Qi, a fiddler. Every evening, the secluded erhu sound that came from the opposite courtyard was transmitted from his hand to my ears. Due to the feeling for art, I couldn't help but change my stubborn state, with some nostalgic expression, said:

"It's you! How could I not know. Your skills, not only now, I have appreciated a lot since I was a child. How are you now?"

"Oh, don't mention it. Now, now, now it's nothing."

"Nothing? Aren't you playing the erhu in the theater?"

"I haven't done that job for two years."

Old Qi's eyes were a little gloomy, like a cloud covering his mood. Indeed, I have also heard people say that this year, he had only been invited to one cold place—the Binyan Hualou, by a few amateur opera performers. His previous glory had disappeared. He became a violinist of those "trio" on the road. Sometimes, it was difficult to find a partner. Was it because he was old? Or was it because of other reasons that he lost the favor of the old patrons?

"I can't get along, Sixth Master. They're new—they say they're new, and they see us as old. The old patrons also love new things, composing new tunes, going to Harbin, running to Hong Kong, Shanghai. Leaving me here unchanged, one is reluctant to part with the cheap coal noodles in Beiping, and the other is that there is an old mother at home. I just fell down like this, isn't that right?"

"You are too humble, opening a class and recruiting students."

"What are you talking about! It's easy to say, but it's not easy..."

Old Qi seemed to suddenly have an unpleasant thought. He held the tofu and walked past me, saying at the end:

"See you tomorrow!"

This time I left Beiping in 1933 to find a few friends to do a small thing. Who knew that four years later, I would still return to my secluded old residence. I still live in the front yard—the room with two jujube trees next to the window. I started doing some editing work—extracting the main ideas from the original text and writing a booklet about the main trends of modern criticism.

I hope to regain my early inspiration in that light corner and write prose poems. But I can't hear that elegant erhu sound anymore. In the past, this erhu sound always made me feel nostalgic, dreamy, and sleepless, but now it is silent, and I can't help but guess—oh, Old Qi, you are silent... you have not abandoned art, or did you move?

The servant Lao Tian told me when he was asked once:

"Old Qi is in jail, and hasn't come out yet. The year before last, he opened a small grocery store and lost hundreds of dollars; he returned to his hometown to sell land, and got into a lawsuit. He lost the lawsuit and was given... alas, what a pity, that good Xipi skill!"

Writer Anecdotes

Voltaire

— Gan Si

In 1771, when the great French writer Voltaire arrived in England, he discovered that the English people intensely hated the French. Therefore, walking on the streets of London was a dangerous activity for his life. One day, as he was strolling, a group of angry Englishmen shouted, "Kill him, hang this Frenchman!"

Voltaire stood firm, facing them, and loudly said, "Gentlemen of England! You want to kill me because I am French! But I am unfortunate and cannot be English. Isn't this punishment severe enough?"

The crowd, upon hearing this, couldn't help but cheer and safely escorted Voltaire back to his own residence.

An Inch of Land, An Inch of Blood 120

— Ye Jingfeng

Why did Tsurumi come to Matsushima? It's obvious that his plan has failed. He thought he could use the Black Dragon Society to passively reduce hindering forces and perhaps actively obtain more accurate information to explore the secrets of the "Seven Sealed Letters." Who knew that the Black Dragon Society would give him a Pingzi, a rather formidable opponent; moreover, judging from the past dozen hours, it seems like he is still a love demon, a persistent entanglement that is not easy to escape.

From the Konoe residence, he saw that Konoe, this merit-hungry and bloodthirsty demon, was not as easy to deal with as he had imagined. Besides, he originally knew that the Fifth Column was quite formidable, but he never dreamed that there would be such vigilant and agile figures among them. There was also that Elder Aoki, simply an incredible magician, who could grasp metaphysical power and manipulate people's psychology. He still doesn't know what their views are on this invasion war, but if they happen to support annexing the entire Asia and want to be world overlords, thinking like those demons, then this kind of magic group is also a huge obstacle. In other words, Tsurumi wanting to use his own strength and that of a few comrades to handle this major event of revealing the "Secret Gears" is equivalent to climbing a tree to catch fish.

Furthermore, listening to Pingzi's tone, there are many factions in Tokyo's political, military, and business circles, each with considerable power, and they are making a big deal out of his insignificant participation in the Black Dragon Society. It seems that, even before taking action, his plan is destined to fail. Moreover, his physical exhaustion in the past two days is also a major factor leading him to despair. Therefore, he temporarily put everything down and ran to Matsushima in a puff of smoke. Madam Koyori and Kikuko have the mixed warmth and understanding of a mother, a lover, and a confidante, and the quiet and elegant location and residence are enough to eliminate the bad mood in his heart.

He dozed off for a while, daydreamed for a while, and felt hungry, so he put on his slippers and went downstairs. It was Kikuko who first discovered Tsurumi coming downstairs, as if she had been waiting at the bottom of the stairs. She first gave Tsurumi a casual greeting, asking if he had slept well, and then, with her sweet and crisp voice, called into the half-open room, "Mom, Yu-ge is coming downstairs." Madam Koyori also answered from the kitchen, "Kiku, quickly open the door to the Buddhist hall." Then, the old lady, who was over sixty but didn't look old, rushed out of the kitchen with a kind smile on her face.

Kikuko took the lead, opened the door to the Buddhist hall, and stepped aside to let Tsurumi and her mother enter the hall. This was a small room covered with tatami mats, inside which oil lamps and Zhilan incense were already lit. In the center of the shrine was a Buddha statue, and on the altar below were several frames, each containing an enlarged photograph. One was a posthumous photo of Koyori Keita, Kikuko's father; another was a photo of Meizi, Tsurumi's adoptive mother.

Madam Koyori and Kikuko accompanied Tsurumi to pay respects and pray for blessings in the Buddhist hall, and then they walked together to the living room, where they greeted each other again; there was no nagging or triviality. At this time, Kikuko showed her housekeeping skills, first serving Tsurumi to sit down, and then instructing the maid to serve dishes and warm wine. The place was filled with warmth: Madam Koyori sat near the window, watching Tsurumi drink wine with a smile, and said some polite words that didn't make people feel uncomfortable: "I seemed to have a premonition, I didn't intend to go to the market today, and I didn't intend to buy these foods. I don't know if your taste has changed for the small dried fish you usually like...?"

Kikuko poured wine cup by cup, occasionally interjecting a light and elegant joke, "Yu-ge's taste won't change much; look, his first chopstick is a slice of fish, the second chopstick is also a slice of fish, and the third chopstick is still a slice of fish."

Presented to Dr. Mei Lanfang

— Zhao Chengbo

Four Seven-Character Quatrains with a Preface

Dr. Mei Lanfang is good at music, singing, and dancing, and is a leader of the opera world of our time. During the war, he was trapped in enemy territory and could not escape, so he grew a beard and refused to perform; his determination to destroy his appearance and swallow charcoal, vowing to serve the country, was not much different from that of Tang musician Lei Haiqing. After the victory, he performed The Imperial Concubine Assassinates the Tiger in Shanghai, and a ticket cost ten thousand gold, with people rubbing shoulders as if going to the market. The drama was perfect, and its appeal was appropriate! The mirror reflects the faithfulness of Zhang Shengmin and the integrity of a martyr; the empty flute case shows even more the ambition to care for one's homeland. I wrote four seven-character quatrains to praise him.

It is when the soldiers break through the enemy, that the song and dance of Neon Clothes remind one of before the lanterns; the Peking Opera circle has its own sad stories, and Mei Lanfang has been trapped for ten years.

Ghost fires burn autumn graves, mounds of earth stretch for ten thousand; the rise and fall are like a dream, the water flows long; don't say that no one gets old in war, the doctor is now white-haired.

Red powder and blue shirt express patriotism, a turtledove's appearance and a swan's face show shame at stealing life; the talented person has passed away, and the tortoise year is old, who else recognizes the name?

Ten years of desolation in the song of the brothel, today the smiling voices in the tower are harmonious; I beg the Lang not to grow old easily, the Central Plains is still the land of the Han.

Free Talk

Lament for the Shantytowns

— Shao Fu

Policies must be implemented, and we wholeheartedly support them. The authorities have a practical spirit and a wise plan, they want to do things and are willing to do things, and we also admire them very much; and we can understand and sympathize with all the difficulties and obstacles encountered in the implementation of policies. However, regarding the demolition of shantytowns, we would like to suggest getting through this harsh winter and holding it again next spring, that is, postponing the implementation for two months. I wonder if this humble opinion can be heard?

For the safety of four million people, sacrifice forty thousand shantytowns, even if it is not to such an exact degree, but the construction of the urban area has its own overall plan, and besides, these forty thousand shantytowns are by no means a sacrifice, just asking them to move to non-restricted construction areas. So in principle, we absolutely support it, without a doubt.

Why do we ask to postpone the implementation for two months? That is really for the sake of humanity. This year, all industries have felt depressed, and the middle and lower classes have felt the economic pressure. Adding to the severe cold, the end of winter, demolition and construction, and large-scale construction will not only increase the financial burden, but also make people feel embarrassed in terms of manpower. If you and I are one of these forty thousand households, in this desolate and declining year, what kind of sad shadow will you and I's emotions be covered with!

Human touch! We'd better take care of it a little bit!

Of course, we know very well the seriousness of the authorities' handling of this matter, and we also know that the shantytown residents will definitely obey the orders and follow the regulations, and there will be no problems. Maybe we are too emotional, but if we let these shantytowns live through this harsh winter, wouldn't it be more humane?

It's just a woman's kindness!

Ten Years Ago Today in Tokyo

— Xiaomai

…Remembering an important day in history…

Ten years ago today, Chairman Chiang was in distress in Xi'an. It took thirteen days for him to escape danger and return to Nanjing. Before leaving Shaanxi, Chairman Chiang gave instructions to Zhang and Yang, saying, "This resolution of the Xi'an Incident is related to the survival of China's fifty-year history and the survival of the Republic of China." Ten years of history have proved that these two "prophetic" comments are not exaggerated.

When the "Double Twelfth" Incident occurred, the author was staying in Tokyo. The situation at that time is still vaguely remembered.

According to historical records, the "Double Twelfth Incident" occurred at 5 a.m. before dawn that day. That morning, the Xi'an Telegraph Bureau was already under surveillance by the defense forces, so the news could not be transmitted. The first extra edition in Tokyo, I remember, was published before the regular evening newspaper, which seemed to have been sent from Nanjing. As far as I know afterwards, many of the telegrams from the newspapers at that time and later were deleted by the Japanese authorities, so what was left was too short to be shortened. After the evening newspaper at about 5 p.m., there was also an extra edition from a certain newspaper.

The Enemy Rejoices

From then until Chiang's escape from danger and return to Nanjing on "December 25," the reporters stationed in China by major newspapers in Tokyo were ordered by the head office to compete for reports. Even the city's field reporters desperately interviewed external reactions. At that time, the Chinese Embassy in Japan and Ambassador Xu Shiying in Azabu District were naturally the first targets, but Xu kept his mouth shut and the reporters gained nothing. As far as I know afterwards, the information successively received by the "Kasumigaseki" (Ministry of Foreign Affairs) and "Miyakesaka" (Ministry of the Army) in Tokyo, Japan, was comparable to that of the embassy!

When the city's field reporters had nothing to write or record, the "Yomiuri Shimbun," which had risen in Tokyo and engaged in a "battle for supremacy" with the two major overlords, "Asahi" and "Mainichi," actually interviewed the dormitory of students studying in Japan. A certain student studying in Tokyo replied, "What we know is as much as what is recorded in the newspapers." This sentence (a bit like "diplomatic language," but it is indeed the truth) was unexpectedly published on the front page of the city news, and several photos were inserted.

From the evening of the 12th, I clearly remember that Tokyo's teahouses, small restaurants, and bathhouses all took this as a topic and as the center of conversation.

The main Japanese military and political figures were naturally very "concerned" about the situation at that time. The author happened to take a "metered car" on a matter of business late on the 13th, passing near the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs! I saw that they were still brightly lit, which was different from usual. It was not until the morning of the 14th that I read the newspaper that I knew that the main Japanese figures had held a long meeting there for four or five hours, discussing the so-called "countermeasures," whose consistent motive was to "see if they could fish in troubled waters and take advantage of the situation."

The next day, the leaders of the Japanese army and navy also held a joint meeting, deciding on the following two so-called "principles": (1) Take self-defense measures when necessary; (2) Be vigilant and observe quietly. Isn't this a "fishing" measure? At that time, the Minister of Foreign Affairs was Arita, the Minister of the Army was Terauchi, and the Minister of the Navy was Nagano.

After the incident, Ambassador Xu's first official contact with the Japanese authorities was the day after Chiang Ting-wen returned to Luoyang from Shaanxi on the 18th. This conversation lasted for more than fifty minutes. At that time, Foreign Minister Arita even shamelessly requested, "I hope to obtain some special news about the Xi'an Incident in a private capacity."

The Japanese ambassador to China at that time was Kawagoe, but he had left Beijing and lived in Shanghai as early as December 5 because the Sino-Japanese negotiations had come to an end. It was not until the 19th that he returned to Beijing from Shanghai under the instruction of the "Ministry of Foreign Affairs." However, regardless of whether Kawagoe was in Beijing or Shanghai, the Tokyo side obtained the information in the same quick and detailed way during these thirteen days.

Interestingly, the views expressed by the head of the agency, Doihara, were clear and blunt: "Japan really should quickly re-examine China."

Disappointed

No matter how beautiful the diplomatic rhetoric is, and no matter how slippery the newspaper editorials are, it cannot be denied that the Japanese warlords wanted to take advantage of the situation at that time. The author still remembers that after "Double Twelfth," the sharp decline in the Tokyo stock market, cotton cloth transactions, and rayon prices can prove what the Japanese people were imagining in their hearts. Isn't this thinking of expanding the conflict between the two sides and causing a major war on the "wishful thinking"?

On the evening of December 25, Tokyo newspapers also issued extra editions, and many of them included photos of Chiang. That night was supposed to be a night of celebration, but on this night, many financial and military leaders were greatly disappointed. Because: what they had hoped for had been shattered. Only some people in the stock market made a fortune.

On that night, many students studying abroad did celebrate wildly, and some almost stayed up all night. But it is doubtful what they were celebrating for. On that night, how many people knew that the Sino-Japanese War, which would begin seven months later, had already planted the fuse and the seeds of victory nine years later?

Learn from the Children!

12 and 13

— Momo

Some people believe that "thirteen" is the most unlucky number, because at the Last Supper of Jesus, including Judas who killed Jesus, there were exactly thirteen people at the table.

Therefore, some people say: The reason why the "Xi'an Incident" was able to be resolved peacefully that year was because the incident occurred on the "twelfth" and not the "thirteenth."

But he forgot that the number of days from the incident to the rescue to the escape of General Chiang, that is, from the twelfth to the twenty-fifth, was exactly thirteen days!

Some people also say this: On the evening of the eleventh, Shao Yuan-chong, Yang Hu-cheng, Chen Cheng... and others ate at a table of thirteen people in Xi'an. Therefore, Shao suffered an accident at dawn on the twelfth.

And Zhang Xueliang "Young Marshal" did not attend the banquet that night, didn't he later receive a pardon?

Shao Yuan-chong stayed in room 113 of the "Xijing Guest House" in Xi'an that night. The place of martyrdom was again "thirteen"!

Only Mr. Enders flew to Shaanxi on the thirteenth to mediate, and this "thirteen" was a good omen.

And today, the "Guest House" has changed this room stained with historical bloodstains to room 130.

But the Arabic numerals are still written as "thirteen", but there is a "zero" after "thirteen", indicating that the戾气has disappeared!

[12], Eventful Day

In terms of months, May is the month with the most anniversaries of the year. But in terms of day order, the "twelfth day" of each month seems to be an "eventful day."

Today's twelfth is one example. Ten years ago, today, the twelfth, some people made a big mess, almost causing a big trouble.

According to the author's knowledge, other months with the twelfth as a holiday include:

February 12th, North-South Unification Anniversary

March 12th, Anniversary of the death of Mr. Sun Yat-sen.

April 12th, Anniversary of the Qing Party in the thirteenth year of the Republic of China.

November 12th, Anniversary of the birth of Mr. Sun Yat-sen.

December 12th, Xi'an Incident Anniversary.

Also, Chairman Chiang escaped from Xi'an and returned to Nanjing on December 25th, which is both the anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising and the world-wide "Christmas". (Ink)

Women First?

— Chen Zhong

Our country has always valued men over women. Most parents think of their daughters as "other people's" people. Once they are married, they are even more "unwanted goods", so-called "daughters who are married off are like water that is poured out." Although we can exceptionally see records of valuing women in old books, it is after all an exception. Fortunately, in recent years, the idea of equal rights for men and women has been highly praised, and society has taken notice of women and looked at them with new eyes. Especially in cities, women are the most glamorous, and snobbish parents value women even more. Daughters are their cash cows, and sons are the ones who are useless!

In the "upper class" society of Shanghai, where Chinese and foreigners live together, we often hear the slogan "Women First" - Ladies First - is it an international saying since it is translated in both Chinese and English? Therefore, many people believe in it: smoking requires women's permission, you have to take off your hat when you see a woman, and women get priority getting on and off the bus, entering and exiting the room. Even in some universities, female students are first, sitting in the first row in the lecture hall, which has become an immutable habit.

The National Assembly Representatives did not set up separate young and old representatives based on age, but there are women representatives as a separate group. Are women not worthy of being social elites and party representatives...? Are women representatives only representatives because they are women? It seems that they are also influenced by "women first." Is "women first" an insult to women or respect for women?

The trend of "women first" comes entirely from Europe and the United States. We Chinese are just "copying" it, but we don't know that "women first" is a contradiction in Europe and the United States.

Let's take English as an example: except for the phrase Ladies and Gentlemen when speaking, where women come first. If you write a letter to Mr. and Mrs. Wang, they always write Mr. and Mrs. Wang and not Mrs. and Mr. Wang, with women in the back, this is the first. In articles, especially Americans often like to use He or She or His or Her, with men always on top and women below, this is the second. As for the word "mankind" in English is Mankind and not Womankind, it can be seen that men are enough to represent humanity, while women are not enough. Calling "people" Human Being instead of Huwoman Being is also the same situation. Language is the main feature representing a nation, and there are so many contradictions in English and American (the birthplace of women first); what about others?

B: "Isn't it? China has plenty of bacteria!"

— Guo Hong

One day, a young and energetic young man suddenly developed a strange disease. His left hand hit his right hand, and his right hand hit his left hand, hitting them until the skin was torn and the flesh was open, but he still hit them harder and harder. The people around shook their heads, puzzled.

Milk and Biscuits - A Blessing Too Thin to Enjoy

— Xiao

The National Assembly Representatives moved the refreshment expenses to relieve the Nanjing refugees, and the relief items included "milk" and "biscuits."

But strangely, the refugees didn't care about "milk and biscuits," but asked for "pancakes and fried dough sticks" - is it that milk and biscuits are not as "nutritious" as pancakes and fried dough sticks? It also makes people a little confused!

Logically, beggars can't be choosers, so how can there be a reason to not want biscuits but to want pancakes? Guessing, I'm afraid it's a question of whether you can get full. Although milk and biscuits have lovely names, the amount each person gets may not be more substantial than two pancakes and two fried dough sticks!

Wool Blanket Weeping and Crying Out for Injustice

— Xiao Kangshi

Please Investigate the Truth Thoroughly

The case of the public educators' arrest of the wool blanket for bringing it to justice has been published in the previous eight issues of this magazine. It really contains injustice that cannot be extended, and the suffering is difficult to declare; the arrest warrant is issued, how terrified! Therefore, I have to plead the following information to public officials and others. I hope you will appreciate it, in order to reveal the sunken injustice - investigate the truth thoroughly, in order to clarify where the responsibility lies!

The wool blanket and the silkworm body have an agreement, and the price is based; the original plan was to always accompany public educators throughout their lives, growing old together, to show tenderness -, but the original media materials supply organization, harbored the idea of ​​reversing, and intended to sell the wool blanket for its appearance at a high price; it was not voluntary, but forced! The body cannot be the master, containing this sunken injustice! I have never dared to have distant faith and righteousness, and give birth to two ambitions! It is really the original media that is playing tricks and profiting from it!

Now the wool blanket has lost its body to others, and Bai Bi has a stain! People's words are terrifying, and I want to jump out of the fire pit! I have repeatedly negotiated with the original media, sincerely from the good (public educators), but the cunning matchmaker is doing evil, and even tempting me to redeem myself at a high price! With the fragile appearance of the wool blanket, I dare not compete; I can only contain injustice and weep, who will pity me? If public educators and others miss the tenderness and affection of the wool blanket? It is better to sue the cunning matchmaker for turning his back and deceiving the wool blanket into falling into Pingkang! Once there is a day of public trial, the wool blanket should go to court to testify, in order to punish the traitor and express the anger of the crowd. I urgently weep injustice as above, I hope you will thoroughly investigate, it is really very hard!
