Shanghai Cross Section

The Organization of Beggars 18

— Huang Jiajin

True and False Passengers

The local beggar gangs are stuck in the Shanghai market. Although they try hard to survive, they are ubiquitous, but they are always disheveled and haggard. It is not the ambition of a man. Therefore, the general young and strong people decided to find another way, which is in line with the original color of their "men's ambition is in all directions." These beggars, with lofty aspirations, actually went far away and began their travel career. This is the new route of the so-called "flying kite" in the beggar gang. However, this kind of livelihood still does not get rid of fraudulent methods. "Flying kite" means walking on boats. Shanghai has convenient transportation, and the water and land routes are as dense as cobwebs. The local beggar gangs can use the opportunity to travel to and from various places all year round without spending a penny. Moreover, every time they go out, they are sure to "tease the rake" (getting money). Without the real ability to stand alone, how can you build a family empty-handed?

Performance on the Boat

These people pretend to be passengers on the boat every day, and their clothes are quite neat, not revealing the true colors. When the passengers are complete and the boat leaves, they begin their crying and laughing skills. First, they greet the passengers next to them, and gradually talk about their own affairs. Then, they fabricate their past identity, such as being a businessman in their hometown, but unexpectedly suffered a disaster, the shop went bankrupt, and his wife died and his children were scattered. It seems that all the suffering in life is concentrated on one person. So the passengers on the boat gathered to ask questions, respectfully listening to his speech. Chinese people have always been honest and generous, especially when they have plenty of time on the journey and like to meddle in other people's business. Everyone meets by chance, and they feel particularly close. Soon, everyone spreads the word, and everyone can't help but feel pity. The beggar thinks that the good opportunity should not be missed, and asks the public for alms. At this time, everyone will generously donate money. In a short time, the collected number is considerable. When the ticket inspector comes, he finds that there is no ticket. The passengers will intercede for him and give him preferential treatment. Therefore, the beggar not only gets a free ride, but also returns fully loaded. The next day, he takes another ship back to Shanghai, and can repeat the tragedy again. After a long time, the crew will inevitably see through the trick, so they have to bribe them to silence them. Sometimes, they even need to distribute lubrication to be safe. But no matter what, as long as they travel a few times a month, the total income is far better than their peers on Zhengzhu Street.

This kind of "flying kite" drama is most common on ships traveling on the Yangtze River. The second is on sea vessels traveling to Ningbo Shaoxing. It turns out that the Shanghai Ningbo Shaoxing Association has regulations that poor fellow villagers who have fallen on Shanghai can be given a free boat ticket back home by the Association. The beggar pretends to be a fellow villager, but his goal is not the boat ticket, but to get a letter of introduction. The letter states that they can receive two yuan of ocean (the real situation before the war) from a certain place after returning home. And on the boat, they can rely on wonderful performances to get great benefits. Who would have thought that the Association's preferential treatment would instead create a slippery business for the beggars?

Station Drama

In addition to the "sea mountain" (ship) on the waterway, they also operate at the railway station. People in the gang call the train "flying centipede." But on the train, they can't ask passengers for help, because the feelings of passengers in the same car are very weak, not as cordial as the passengers on the boat who "share the same boat." Moreover, a fourth-class ticket is definitely not free. After they get off at their destination, they begin their crying and laughing performance when the passengers are crowded at the station. Asking the passengers for assistance. Several buses come and go at a station every day. Passengers are also constantly flowing, and the beggar can be active at Station A one day, and then take the bus to Station B the next day. Although they are dusty and tired, the income is considerable. This is the new route for the "flying kite" gang to leave the dock.

If I Were to Form a Party

— Gu

If I were to form a party, first and foremost, I would choose the best name: "Equal Freedom Democratic Party." Perhaps some might think the name is too long, but because it needs to fit practical needs, it must be this way.

Then, I must publish a declaration, stating that our party grew from the grassroots, therefore, we can certainly represent true public opinion. The party's policy is based on "Equal Freedom Democracy," so it will certainly always consider the people. This declaration does not need to be long, but the words "the people" must be mentioned as often as possible.

As long as we have a few "cadres," then I will certainly claim that our party members are spread throughout China, with an astonishing number – say, our party already has 200,000,001 members. In this way, it can prove that our party represents the "majority" of "public opinion."

With such a large number of party members, we should of course do something, because the purpose of our party is "everything for the people"!

Therefore, I will request the government to appoint our party members to positions within the National Government organization. The head of the Executive Yuan is needed, the head of the Legislative Yuan is needed, and of course, the Minister of Finance is also needed! The more, the better. When writing articles, one should insert the phrase: "Willing to be an official."

If the government agrees, then we'll talk about it after we become officials; (our party has a spirit of enterprise!) If it cannot be completely satisfactory, then this is because the government is not democratic, and we can organize ourselves.

My party will surely flourish, party members will surely have official positions, and, "everything for the people"! Should party members "not be suitable"?

Talking About Xi'an on the Twelfth of December

— Ye Zi

The Xi'an dialect has many local phonetic components, which are quite interesting to outsiders. Xi'an people say "what place" as "yi ya da" (　　), like a Shanghai shirt trademark. Also, Xi'an calls "there" as "wu da" (ua), which is like the Japanese surname "Uda" in pronunciation. Other interesting examples include calling "head" as "duo la" or "sha."

The word "I" in Chang'an, generally has three pronunciations. One is "wu" (ngo), like the Cantonese pronunciation of "I". The second is "ngai", as far as I know, the Pearl River Delta also has this pronunciation. The third is "× ya" (wa), which is exactly the same as the ancient Japanese word for "I" which is pronounced as "wa". These three pronunciations have considerable value in phonological studies.

A certain Western medicine store in Xi'an has a telephone number of "606", and the number of its branch is "914".

There is a cinema in Xi'an called "Epang Palace." Someone asked him, when will you be showing the film "Burning Epang Palace"?

In late autumn and early winter in Xi'an, there is an inexpensive and delicious snack called "Persimmon Cake," which is made by mashing ripe red persimmons, mixing them with flour, and then deep-frying them until fragrant. The taste is delicious, not inferior to Western "cooked cakes" or Cantonese "steamed cakes".

A week ago, I saw an old villager on the street with his nose painted red, wearing a sheepskin coat inside out, with the white wool facing outwards. He was also riding a donkey backwards, that is, with his back facing the donkey's head and his face facing the donkey's buttocks. Most amusingly, he also had a chamber pot (of course, brand new!) hanging from his shoulders with a red string. Before the procession, there were several people playing music and carrying offerings of tea, fruit, and snacks for the gods. It was said to be a local custom of offering thanks to the gods for the birth of a baby boy to an old man. However, whether this gentleman was following Xi'an customs or if this custom was brought from another town, was not investigated, and I dare not make a reckless judgment.

In Xi'an, the newlywed "teasing the bride" custom involves all sorts of pranks, more than half of which are semi-forced and semi-willingly making the newlyweds kiss in public, which shows that "rouge" is not an imported product.

"Dream of the Red Chamber" describes the sights and objects of Western Capital, and many of the place names and temple names mentioned in it still exist today. For example, the rich store opened by Aunt Xue and Wang Xifeng's family, is repeatedly mentioned in the book as being on "West Street" next to the "Drum Tower." This building and street name still exist today, and is one of the crossroads in the city center, but the "Drum Tower" has been without drums for a long time. On the top of the building, there is only a huge horizontal plaque with the inscription "Sound Heard in Heaven." Since the War of Resistance, the building has been equipped with an air-raid siren, a coincidental concurrence.

The lowest-level brothel district in Xi'an, "Duck Pit," is like calling prostitutes "wild chickens" elsewhere, or Cantonese people calling them "cat caves," suggesting prostitutes are not human, but domestic fowl, which is the same thing. A certain gentleman wrote "Lament of Duck Pit," and here are a few lines excerpted below:

"...

There are no ducks or eggs in the pit,

The pit is full of pitiful people.

Ducks are sometimes human.

Ducks float in the green water of the pond,

In the Duck Pit, the body is scorched by fire.

Ducks eat fish and shrimp but don't eat ducks,

In the world, only people eat people!

..."
